The Obligatory Truthfulness of Prophets
Dardeer defines truthfulness for prophets and presents two proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of prophetic truthfulness (sidq) and the rational proof that makes it obligatory.

Core Idea
Truthfulness is non-optional for prophets; God's miracles affirm their words.

This lesson examines a foundational attribute of prophethood: truthfulness. Imam Dardeer defines what it means for a prophet to be truthful and provides both scriptural and logical evidence. The core argument shows that if prophets could lie, then God's confirmation of them through miracles would entail a contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and its translation to grasp Dardeer's concise argument.
2
Understand the definition of sidq
Notice that truthfulness is defined as correspondence between what is said and reality.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Reflect on verse 53:3 as evidence that the Prophet's speech is not from personal desire.
4
Analyze the logical proof
Follow the chain: God confirms by miracle → if prophet could lie, God would confirm a liar → impossible for God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصدق أي: في دعواهم الرسالة، في تبليغهم الأحكام، وهو مطابقة حكم الخبر للواقع، قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا يَنطِقُ عَنِ الْهَوَى﴾ ولأنهم لو جاز عليهم الكذب للزم الكذب في خبره تعالى، لأنه تعالى صدقهم بالمعجزة النازلة منزلة قوله: صدق عندي في كل ما يبلغ عني وتصديق الكاذب كذب محض، والكذب على الله محال لأنه نقص، وما أدى إلى المحال محال.
And truthfulness—meaning: in their claim of prophethood, in their conveying of rulings—and it is the correspondence of the judgment of the news with reality. He, exalted, said: {Nor does he speak from [his own] desire} (53:3). And because if lying were possible for them, then lying would necessarily occur in the report of Him, exalted, because He, exalted, confirmed them by the miracle which takes the place of His saying: 'He is truthful with me in everything he conveys from me,' and confirming a liar is pure lying, and lying about God is impossible because it is a deficiency, and that which leads to the impossible is impossible.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of truthfulness (sidq) that is obligatory for prophets. It begins by specifying that truthfulness applies to their claim of prophethood and their conveying of divine rulings. The definition given is that truthfulness is the correspondence of the judgment of the news with external reality. The author then provides two proofs. The first is a textual proof: the Quranic verse {Nor does he speak from [his own] desire} (53:3), which indicates that the Prophet's speech is not from personal whim but from revelation. The second is a logical proof: if prophets could lie, then God's confirmation of them via miracles would be a confirmation of a liar, which would entail lying on God's part—an impossibility. The argument proceeds as: (1) God confirms the prophet's truthfulness through miracles, which function as God's statement 'He is truthful'. (2) If the prophet were a liar, then God would be affirming a lie. (3) Affirming a lie is itself a lie. (4) Lying is impossible for God because it is a deficiency. (5) Therefore, what leads to the impossible is itself impossible. Hence, prophets must be truthful.

Key Terms
الصدق
المعجزة
الكذب
الخبر
الواقع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think truthfulness means never making a mistake or always agreeing with scripture.
Correction: Truthfulness is defined as correspondence with reality (mutabaqat al-khabar lil-waqi), not infallibility in all matters.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Prophetic truthfulness is not just a moral virtue but a logical necessity derived from God's confirmation via miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

This lesson is not just about the Prophet's truthfulness—it is about God's integrity. If you ever find yourself justifying disobedience by saying 'the Prophet was only human', what are you actually saying about God's confirmation? Does your life reflect this high view of prophetic truthfulness?

The Definition of a Miracle (Mu'jiza)
Dardeer defines the miracle with its three conditions and explains each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of a miracle in Islamic theology, including its three essential conditions and what each excludes.

Core Idea
A miracle is not just any wonder — it must break custom, come with a prophetic challenge, and remain unmatched.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer provides the technical definition of a miracle (mu'jiza), distinguishing it from other extraordinary events. Understanding this definition is crucial for grasping how prophethood is verified. Let's examine each condition carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation to get the overall structure of the definition.
Notice the precise wording of each condition.
2
Identify the three conditions
The definition contains three key parts: extraordinary, coupled with challenge, without opposition. Find each in the text.
3
Understand the exclusions
For each condition, note what kind of event it excludes (customary events, karamat/irhasat, sorcery).
The text uses 'احتراز' (safeguard) for each exclusion.
4
Reflect on the example
The example of Ibrahim (fire not burning) shows that a 'matter' can be an omission of a customary effect.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to confirm you can apply the definition.
The question tests the third condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمعجزة: أمر خارق للعادة، مقرون بالتحدّي مع عدم المعارضة. قد خَلَ في قولنا «أمر» الفعلُ والترك، كعدم إخراق النار لإبراهيم الطاقة. وقولنا «خارق» إلخ احتراز من أن يُتَمَسَّك بالعادات. وقولنا «مقرون بالتحدي» أي دعوى الرسالة احتراز من كرامات الأولياء، والإرهاصات وهي ما تقدم بعثة الأنبياء تأسيسا لها. وقولنا «مع عدم المعارضة» احتراز من السحر والشعوذة.
And the miracle: an extraordinary matter, coupled with the challenge (tahaddi), with the absence of opposition. Our saying 'matter' includes action and omission, like the non-burning of the fire for Ibrahim (Abraham) — a breach of custom. Our saying 'extraordinary' etc. is a safeguard against relying on customary events. Our saying 'coupled with the challenge' — meaning the claim of prophethood — is a safeguard against the marvels (karamat) of saints and the irhasat (preparatory signs) which precede the mission of prophets as a foundation for it. And our saying 'with the absence of opposition' is a safeguard against sorcery (sihr) and sleight-of-hand (sha'wadha).
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage defines the miracle (mu'jiza) as a technical term in Islamic theology. The definition consists of three conditions: (1) It is an extraordinary matter (kharq li'l-ada), meaning it breaks the usual pattern of nature. (2) It is coupled with a challenge (tahaddi), which is the claim of prophethood, meaning the miracle occurs as a proof of the prophet's truth. (3) There is no opposition (adam al-mu'arada), meaning no one else can produce something similar. The author then explains each part. 'Matter' includes both actions (like bringing a staff to life) and omissions (like fire not burning Abraham). 'Extraordinary' excludes ordinary events. 'Coupled with challenge' excludes the wonders of saints (karamat) and preparatory signs (irhasat) that happen before prophethood. 'Without opposition' excludes sorcery and sleight-of-hand, which are not truly miraculous but deceptive.

Key Terms
المعجزة
خارق للعادة
التحدي
المعارضة
الكرامات
الإرهاصات
السحر
الشعوذة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any supernatural event is a miracle.
Correction: A miracle must meet three conditions: it must break custom, be linked to a prophetic claim, and be immune to imitation. This excludes other wonders.

Checkpoint
Why is the condition 'with the absence of opposition' (مع عدم المعارضة) included in the definition of a miracle?
A) To exclude natural events
B) To exclude the wonders of saints
C) To exclude sorcery and sleight-of-hand
D) To exclude events that happen before prophethood

Key Takeaway
The definition of a miracle comprises three conditions that together distinguish it from all other extraordinary events.

The Qur'an as the Ultimate Proof of Prophethood
Dardeer proves Muhammad's prophethood by the miracle of the Qur'an and the failure of the Arabs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an's inimitability (i'jaz) and the failure of the Arabs to meet its challenge serve as a definitive proof of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's challenge remains unanswered, proving it is from Allah.

Imam Dardeer presents the central proof of prophethood: the Qur'an itself. He explains that the Prophet's claim is universally known through tawatur, and then focuses on the miracle of the Qur'an. The passage recounts how the Arabs, despite their eloquence, failed to produce anything like it, and how the false prophet Musaylimah's ridiculous attempts only confirm its divine origin.

Guided Path
1
Understand the tawatur of the claim
Read the first part of the passage noting that the Prophet's claim is known by mass transmission, accepted even by disbelievers.
This establishes the historical certainty of the claim.
2
Examine the Qur'anic challenge
Identify the three stages of the challenge: the whole Qur'an, ten surahs, and one surah. Note the Arabs' inability despite their motivation.
The challenge shows the Qur'an's miraculous nature.
3
Analyze Musaylimah's failed opposition
Read the account of Musaylimah's attempts and see how they are laughable and confirm the Qur'an's uniqueness.
This further highlights the Qur'an's inimitability.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this proof is strong: the Arabs were experts in language, yet they failed, and even their best effort was absurd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسيدنا محمد بن عبد الله بن عبد المطلب – صلى الله عليه وسلم وعلى والديه وأولاده وآله وصحبه وأمته – قد ادعى أنه رسول الله إلى الإنس والجن، بل الخلق جميعًا، وأظهر المعجزة على دعواه: أما دعواه الرسالة فقد علم بالتواتر، حتى لا ينكر ذلك مؤمن ولا كافر. وأما إظهار المعجزة فلو جهين: أحدهما: أنه أظهر كتابًا من عند الله تعالى، وتحدى به مع كمال بلاغتهم وقوتهم على معرفة أساليب الكلام، وطلب من إنسهم وجنهم ذلك، فلم يقدروا على المعارضة. قل لئن اجتمعت الإنس والجن على أن يأتوا بمثل هذا القرآن لا يأتون بمثله ولو كان بعضهم لبعض ظهيرا أي معينًا. فتحدى بعشر سور فلم يقدروا، فتحدى بسورة – الصادق بأقصر سورة – فلم يقدروا على المعارضة مع شدة حرصهم على ذلك، حتى خاطروا بمهجهم، وأعرضوا عن المعارضة بالحروف إلى المقارعة بالسيوف. ولم ينقل عن واحد منهم – مع توفر دواعيهم – الإتيان بشيء مما يدانيه، بل جعل الكذاب أن يعارضه، فأتى بخرافات مضحكة، أي إنسان سمعها إلا وضحك وعلم أنها هذيان. كما في معارضته لسورة الكوثر بقوله: «إنا أعطيناك العقعق، فصل لربك وازعق، إن شانئك هو الأبْلَق»، وكما في معارضته سورة الفيل بقوله: «الفيل ما الفيل، وما أدراك ما الفيل، له ذنب طويل ومشفر وتيل». الكذاب هو مسيلمة اللعين وهذه الخرافات تقشعر منها جلود الصالحين، ولا تلتفت إليها نفوس العارفين.
Our master Muhammad son of Abdullah son of Abdul-Muttalib – may Allah bless him and grant him peace and upon his parents and his children and his family and his companions and his nation – indeed claimed that he is the Messenger of Allah to humans and jinn, rather to all creation, and he manifested the miracle in support of his claim. As for his claim of prophethood, it has been known by tawatur (mass transmission), so that no believer nor disbeliever denies that. As for the manifestation of the miracle, it is for two aspects: One of them: that he manifested a Book from Allah Almighty, and challenged with it while they had perfect eloquence and strength in knowing styles of speech, and he requested that from their humans and jinn, so they were unable to produce opposition. Say: 'If humans and jinn gathered to produce the like of this Qur'an, they would not produce its like even if some of them were helpers to others.' That is, assistants. Then he challenged with ten surahs, and they were unable; then he challenged with a surah – the truthful one with the shortest surah – and they were unable to oppose despite their intense eagerness for that, so much so that they risked their lives and turned from opposition with letters to clashing with swords. And it has not been reported from any of them – despite the abundance of motives – that they produced anything that approaches it. Rather, the liar set out to oppose it, and came with ridiculous absurdities, which no human hears except that he laughs and knows that it is nonsense. As in his opposition to Surah al-Kawthar with his saying: 'Indeed We have given you the hoopoe, so pray to your Lord and shout, indeed your enemy is the piebald.' And as in his opposition to Surah al-Fil with his saying: 'The elephant, what is the elephant? And what will make you know what the elephant is? It has a long tail and a trunk and a tayl...' The liar is Musaylimah the accursed, and these absurdities make the skins of the righteous shudder, and the souls of the gnostics do not pay attention to them.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage presents the proof of prophethood of Muhammad (SAW) through the miracle of the Qur'an. It begins by stating that his claim is known by tawatur (mass transmission), universally acknowledged. The miracle is manifested in two aspects. The first and primary is the Qur'an itself: the Prophet issued a challenge (tahaddi) to the Arabs and jinn to produce something like it, despite their mastery of eloquence. They failed, first when challenged with ten surahs, then with even a single surah. Their failure is striking because they were highly motivated to disprove him, to the point of risking their lives in war instead. No one produced anything comparable. The second aspect is the attempted opposition by the liar Musaylimah, who came with absurd nonsense such as his parody of Surah al-Kawthar and Surah al-Fil. These laughable attempts only confirm the unmatched inimitability (i'jaz) of the Qur'an.

Correction: The Qur'an's inimitability is proven by the inability of the most eloquent Arabs to produce anything like it, even a single surah, despite their strong motivation.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an's inimitability, demonstrated by the Arabs' inability to meet its challenge, is a definitive proof of Muhammad's prophethood.

?

The Quranic Miracle and the Failed Challenge
Dardeer presents the Quran as the supreme miracle and the failed attempts to challenge it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran's inimitability serves as a proof of prophethood and how all attempts to challenge it failed.

Core Idea
The Quran's inimitability proved prophethood; no one could match it.

Dardeer explains that the Prophet’s claim to prophethood is supported by the miracle of the Quran. He describes how the Prophet challenged the eloquent Arabs to produce something like it, but they failed despite their utmost effort. This lesson examines that challenge and the failed counterfeits.

Guided Path

Understand the prophetic claim
The Prophet claimed to be a messenger to all creation. This claim is known by mass transmission (tawātur).
Even disbelievers acknowledged he made this claim.
2

صدق الرسول دعواه في الرسالة شرح الخريدة البهية قد ادعى أنه رسول الله إلى الإنس والجن، بل الخلق جميعًا، وأظهر المعجزة على دعواه: أما دعواه الرسالة، فقد علم بالتواتر، حتى لا ينكر ذلك مؤمن ولا كافر. وأما إظهار المعجزة فلوجهين: أحدهما: أنه أظهر كتابًا من عند الله تعالى، وتحدى به مع كمال بلاغتهم وقوتهم على معرفة أساليب الكلام، وطلب من إنسهم وجنهم ذلك، فلم يقدروا على المعارضة قل لئن اجتمعت الإنس والجن على أن يأتوا بمثل هذا القرآن لا يأتون بمثله ولو كان بعضهم لبعض ظهيرا أي: معينًا، فتحدى بعشر سور فلم يقدروا، فتحدى بسورة - الصادق بأقصر سورة - فلم يقدروا على المعارضة مع شدة حرصهم على ذلك، حتى خاطروا بمهجهم، وأعرضوا عن المعارضة بالحروف إلى المقارعة بالسيوف. ولم ينقل عن واحد منهم - مع توفر دواعيهم- الإتيان بشيء مما يدانيه، بل جعل الكذاب أن يعارضه، فأتى بخرفات مضحكة، أي إنسان سمعها إلا وضحك وعلم أنها هذيان، كما في معارضته لسورة الكوثر بقوله: إنا أعطيناك العقعق، فصل لربك وازعق، إن شانئك هو الأبلق، وكما في معارضته سورة الفيل بقوله: الفيل ما الفيل، وما أدراك ما الفيل، له ذنب طويل ومشفر وتيل.
The truthfulness of the Messenger in his claim to the message (risāla). Explanation of al-Kharīda al-Bahiyya. He claimed that he is the messenger of Allah to mankind and jinn, rather to all creation, and he manifested a miracle upon his claim. As for his claim to the message, it is known by tawātur (mass transmission), such that no believer or disbeliever denies that. As for the manifestation of the miracle, it is for two aspects: One of them: that he manifested a book from Allah Almighty, and challenged with it, despite the perfection of their eloquence and their power in knowledge of the styles of speech, and he requested that from their mankind and jinn, but they were unable to oppose. {Say: If mankind and jinn gathered to produce the like of this Quran, they could not produce its like, even if they were helpers of one another} (Quran 17:88) meaning helpers. He challenged with ten chapters, and they were unable; he challenged with a chapter—the truthful with the shortest chapter—and they were unable to oppose despite the intensity of their desire for that, until they risked their lives and turned from opposing with letters to clashing with swords. And it is not transmitted from any one of them—despite the abundance of their motives—that they brought anything approaching it. Rather, the liar (Musaylimah) tried to oppose it, and he brought ridiculous nonsense. Any person who heard it except he laughed and knew it was delirium, as in his opposing Sūrat al-Kawthar with his statement: 'Indeed, We have given you the magpie, so pray to your Lord and caw, indeed your hateful one is the piebald,' and as in his opposing Sūrat al-Fīl with his statement: 'The elephant, what is the elephant? And what will make you know what the elephant is? It has a long tail, a lip, and a rope.'
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is an argument for the truthfulness of the Prophet's claim to prophethood by focusing on the miraculous nature of the Quran. The author begins by stating that the fact that the Prophet claimed to be a messenger to all creation is well-known by tawātur (mass transmission), so no one—believer or disbeliever—denies that he made this claim. Then he points out that the Prophet manifested a miracle to prove his claim. The first of two aspects of this miracle is the Quran itself. The Prophet brought a book from Allah and challenged the Arabs, who were masters of eloquence, to produce something like it. They were unable, even though they were collectively challenged to produce ten chapters, then a single chapter—the shortest one. Despite their intense desire to discredit him, they resorted to swords instead of words. The author adds that no one among them could produce anything even approaching the Quran. He then gives examples of the failed attempts of the 'liar' (Musaylimah), who produced absurd nonsense that everyone laughed at, such as his parody of Sūrat al-Kawthar and Sūrat al-Fīl. Thus, the Quran stands as an irrefutable proof of prophethood.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawātur)
معجزة (mu‘jiza)
التحدي (al-taḥaddī)
المعارضة (al-mu‘āraḍah)
إعجاز (i‘jāz)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Arabs did not try hard enough to challenge the Quran.
Correction: The text emphasizes their intense desire and failure; they risked their lives and resorted to swords, proving they were unable.

Checkpoint
Why did the Arab polytheists abandon trying to match the Quran and instead fight with swords?
A) They were not given enough time.
B) They failed to produce anything like it despite their best efforts.
C) They lost interest in literary competition.
D) The Prophet forbade them from trying.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's inimitability is a clear proof of prophethood, as all attempts to produce something like it failed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the most eloquent Arabs, with all their motivation, could not produce even a single verse like the Quran. Have you ever truly pondered the words of the Quran—not as a ritual, but as a miracle that demands your response? What would it take for you to treat the Quran as the living proof that it is?
?
The liar Musaylimah attempted to imitate the Quran and produced nonsense that made people laugh. Ask yourself: Do I treat the Quran with the reverence it deserves, or have I become so familiar with it that I no longer see its awe-inspiring power? Could it be that my own heart has become like those who hear but do not ponder?
?
The Arabs had every desire to disprove the Prophet, yet they failed. If you were placed in their position, with your full intellect and eloquence, could you produce a single verse like it? This is not a hypothetical—it is a challenge that remains open until today. Does your inability to answer this question not demand that you submit to the One who revealed it?

Miracles Beyond the Quran: Tawātur and Other Proofs
Dardeer enumerates other miracles and asserts their mass transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's other miracles, transmitted en masse, serve as a second proof of prophethood alongside the Quran.

Core Idea
The many miracles of the Prophet are known by mass transmission, making denial irrational.

After establishing the Quran as a miracle, Dardeer now presents additional miracles that reinforce the Prophet's truthfulness. These wonders—from pebbles glorifying God to food multiplying—were witnessed and transmitted by many, creating certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on miracles
Read the Arabic passage and translation, focusing on the list of miracles and the claim of tawātur.
Notice that Dardeer uses the term 'khawāriq al-‘ādāt' for miracles.
2
Understand tawātur vs. āḥād
The passage says the common denominator of miracles is transmitted by tawātur, even if details are isolated. Clarify what tawātur means.
Tawātur imparts certain knowledge.
3
Reflect on the cumulative proof
Think about why listing many miracles strengthens the argument for prophethood beyond a single miracle.
Quantity can overwhelm doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثاني: النبوات ردت بلاغتها دعوى معارضها * رد الغيور يد الجاني عن الحرم ثانيهما: أنه نقل عنه - عليه الصلاة والسلام - من خوارق العادات ما بلغ القدر المشترك من حد التواتر، وإن كان تفاصيلها آحادًا، كتسبيح الحصى في كفه، وتكليم الجمادات والحيوانات، ونبع الماء من الأصابع، وظهور البركة في الأطعمة والأشربة، وغير ذلك ما لا يحصى كثرة. هذا مع ما كان عليه من حسن الخلق، الذي لا يراه أحد إلا ويقطع أنه ليس بكذاب، وإن كان يقع من الصالين العناد. ومن كمال خلقه تمام الحلم والعلم مع كونه ولد في قوم لا يعرفون شيئًا، من غير أن يتعاطى أسباب العلم، ووفور القوة مع قلة أكله جدا، فيقدم حيث تحجم الأبطال، ويقف حيث يفر عند شدة الهول صناديد الرجال، ويثبت على حاله من الدعوى لدى شدائد الأهوال، حتى لم يجد أعداؤه إليه مطعنا في حال من الأحوال، بل شهد له العدو والحبيب بوفور الكمال والإفضال. كل ذلك نقل إلينا بالتواتر، فعلمنا ذلك علمًا ضروريًا، فلا يعاند في ذلك إلا من استحق من الله تعالى شديد النكال.
The second section: The prophethoods. 'Its eloquence repelled the claim of its opponent, as the jealous repels the hand of the aggressor from the sanctuary.' Secondly: that there was transmitted from him—peace and blessings be upon him—from the breaking of customs (khawāriq al-‘ādāt) what reached the common denominator from the level of tawātur (mass transmission), even if its details are isolated (āḥād), such as the glorification of pebbles in his palm, the speaking of inanimate objects and animals, the gushing of water from his fingers, the manifestation of blessing in foods and drinks, and other things too numerous to count. This, along with what he possessed of good character, which no one sees except that he is certain he is not a liar, even if stubbornness occurs from the stubborn ones. And from the perfection of his character is complete forbearance and knowledge, despite his being born among a people who knew nothing, without his having pursued the means of knowledge; and abundance of strength despite very little food; he advances where the heroes are hesitant, and stands where the champions flee at the intensity of terror; and he remains firm in his state of claim during severe terrors, until his enemies found no opportunity to criticize him in any state; rather, both enemy and friend testified to his abundance of perfection and bounty. All of that was transmitted to us by tawātur, so we know it by necessary knowledge (ʿilm ḍarūrī), and none stubbornly opposes it except one who deserves from Allah Almighty severe punishment.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is the second proof of prophethood after the Quranic miracle. It comes under the section heading 'The second section: The prophethoods.' The author begins with a line from the Burda of al-Būṣīrī praising the Quran's eloquence. Then he lists the multitude of other miracles (khawāriq al-‘ādāt) that were transmitted from the Prophet, such as pebbles glorifying God in his hand, inanimate objects and animals speaking, water flowing from his fingers, and food and drink multiplying—all of which are widely transmitted despite some details being known through isolated reports. The author then adds the Prophet's perfect character as a corroborating proof: anyone who sees him can be sure he is not a liar. He elaborates on his perfect forbearance and knowledge despite being unschooled, his strength despite eating very little, his courage in battle where others flee, and his unwavering perseverance despite severe trials. He concludes that all of this is known by tawātur and thus constitutes necessary knowledge (ʿilm ḍarūrī), so that only one deserving of divine punishment would reject it.

Key Terms
خوارق العادات (khawāriq al-‘ādāt)
تواتر (tawātur)
آحاد (āḥād)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the transmission status of these miracles?
A) All details are transmitted by tawātur.
B) The common denominator is tawātur, but details are āḥād.
C) They are all fabricated.
D) Only the Quran is tawātur.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's miracles beyond the Quran are transmitted en masse, providing certain knowledge of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Do you find yourself relying on intellectual proofs or emotional conviction, and which is stronger in your heart? Now, ask yourself: are you willing to base your faith on this cumulative evidence alone, or do you secretly wish for a direct sign?
?
This passage lists miracles like pebbles glorifying and water flowing from fingers. If you had witnessed one of these, would your faith be stronger? Since you haven't, does the mass transmission give you the same level of certainty? Be honest: is your faith built on proofs or on habit?
?
The author emphasizes that the details of miracles are isolated reports, but the common denominator is certain. Are you content with this cumulative evidence, or do you seek more direct signs from Allah in your own life? Reflect on whether you demand miracles before submitting, or accept the proofs already given. What would it take for you to be absolutely certain?

The Prophet's Perfect Character: A Living Proof of Prophethood
Dardeer describes the Prophet's character and concludes it is known by tawātur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's character, known through mass transmission, provides compelling evidence of his truthfulness.

Core Idea
The Prophet's character is so perfect that no one could doubt his sincerity.

Beyond miracles, Dardeer points to the Prophet's character as an additional, self-evident proof. His forbearance, knowledge despite being unlettered, courage, and steadfastness all testify to his truthfulness. This character was witnessed by all, friend and foe, and transmitted to us massively.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on character

These are not just moral but also intellectual and physical.
2
Analyze the argument
Why does Dardeer consider character a proof? Because anyone observing him would be certain he is not a liar.
This relies on the human ability to judge character.
3
Understand tawātur and necessary knowledge
All of this was transmitted by tawātur, producing necessary knowledge (ʿilm ḍarūrī).
Necessary knowledge is immediate and certain.
4
Reflect on the consequence
Denying this evidence merits severe punishment from Allah.

Prophethood of Others and Finality of Muhammad
Dardeer explains that prophethood of other prophets is known from revelation and that Muhammad is the final prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the prophethood of previous prophets is established through the Qur'an and Sunnah, and that Muhammad (peace be upon him) is the final prophet, with no new prophethood after him.

Core Idea
Muhammad is the last prophet; no new prophet comes after him.

Imam Dardeer explains that the prophethood of earlier prophets like Adam is known from divine revelation, not reason alone. He also affirms that the Qur'an and Sunnah clearly establish Muhammad as the final prophet. This lesson will help you understand these foundational beliefs about prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation to grasp the flow.
Notice the two main parts: prophethood of others and finality of Muhammad.
2
Identify the source of knowledge for other prophets
The text says prophethood of others is known 'by the Book and the Sunnah'. Reflect on why this is important.
It is through revelation, not reason alone.
3
Understand the implications of being the last prophet
The passage states Muhammad is 'the last of the prophets', meaning no new prophethood after him.
This is a core belief in Islam.
4
Reflect on the misconception
The passage clearly rules out any new prophet, but some confuse saints or reformers with prophets. Understand the difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما نبوة غيره كآدم فمن بعده، فقد علم بالكتاب والسنة، وأثنى عليهم الله تعالى في كتابه بقوله ورسلا مبشرين ومنذرين وغير ذلك، فيجب لهم ما يجب له عليه الصلاة والسلام، والبعض قد عينه الكتاب والبعض لم يعينه. وقد ثبت بالكتاب والسنة أنه آخر النبيين، فلا تبتدأ نبوة بعده عليه الصلاة والسلام.
And as for the prophethood of others like Adam and those after him, it is known by the Book and the Sunnah. Allah Almighty praised them in His Book by His saying: 'And messengers as bearers of good news and warners' (Quran 4:165) and other verses. So what is incumbent upon him—peace and blessings be upon him—is incumbent upon them. Some of them are specified by the Book, and some are not specified. And it has been established by the Book and the Sunnah that he is the last of the prophets, so no prophethood is initiated after him, peace and blessings be upon him.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a brief statement about the status of other prophets and the finality of Muhammad's prophethood. The author asserts that the prophethood of prophets before Muhammad—such as Adam and those after him—is known through the Qur'an and Sunnah. The Qur'an praises them in verses like 'messengers as bearers of good news and warners.' Therefore, the same obligations that apply to Muhammad (such as belief in his prophethood, love, and respect) also apply to them, as all prophets are brothers. Some of these prophets are explicitly named in the Qur'an, while others are not mentioned by name. Finally, the author confirms that it is established in the Qur'an and Sunnah that Muhammad is the last of the prophets (khatam al-nabiyyīn); no new prophet can come after him.

Key Terms
نبوة (nubuwwa)
آخر النبيين (ākhir al-nabiyyīn)
الكتاب والسنة (al-kitāb wa al-sunna)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that saints or reformers can become prophets after Muhammad.
Correction: The passage clearly states 'no prophethood is initiated after him,' meaning no new prophet can come, regardless of spiritual rank.

Checkpoint
How do we know that Muhammad is the last prophet?
A) By rational proof alone.
B) By the consensus of scholars.
C) By the Book and the Sunnah.
D) By the statements of earlier prophets.

Key Takeaway
Muhammad is the last prophet, and no new prophet can come after him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe that Muhammad is the last prophet. Yet, in your daily decisions, do you treat any person, trend, or ideology as if it brings new guidance that overrides or adds to his teaching? Where specifically are you vulnerable to that?
?
The passage says that what is obligatory towards Muhammad is also obligatory towards all prophets. Is there any prophet—like Moses, Jesus, or those you know less about—toward whom you feel less respect or love? Ask yourself why, and repent.
?
If no prophethood can begin after Muhammad, then what about the 'inspirations' you chase from social media influencers, self-help gurus, or even your own unchecked desires? How can you audit your heart today to ensure you are not seeking guidance from a source that conflicts with his finality?

Proof of Prophethood through Miracles and Perfect Character
A presentation of miraculous events and character traits as proofs of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the twofold proof of Muhammad's prophethood: his extraordinary miracles and his impeccable character, both transmitted by mass testimony (tawatur) yielding necessary knowledge.

Core Idea
Miracles and character: two unassailable proofs for Muhammad's prophethood.

Imam Dardeer presents two categories of evidence that establish the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) beyond doubt. The first is the countless miraculous events (kharq al-'adat) that were witnessed and transmitted. The second is his perfect character, which even his enemies could not deny. Both lines of evidence have reached us through widespread, continuous transmission (tawatur), producing certain knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on miracles and character
Read the Arabic passage once to get an overview. Then read the translation. The passage first lists miracles, then describes character traits.
Notice the examples: pebbles glorifying, water from fingers, blessing in food.
2
Identify the two proofs
The author explicitly mentions two proofs: (1) miraculous occurrences (خوارق العادات) and (2) good character (حسن الخلق). Identify each in the text.
The character description includes forbearance, knowledge, courage, and steadfastness.
3
Understand the role of tawatur
The author states that all of this was transmitted by tawatur (mass transmission), resulting in necessary knowledge (علم ضروري). This means the knowledge is certain and undeniable.
Even if details are ahad (singular reports), the overall proof is mutawatir.
4
Reflect on the strength of the proof
Consider why character alone can prove truthfulness: anyone who sees the Prophet's character would conclude he is not a liar. Combined with miracles, the proof is overwhelming.
The author emphasizes that even enemies testified to his perfection.

وما أحسن قولَ شَرفِ الدين البوصيري في البُرْدة: القسم الثاني: النبوات ردت بلاغتها دعوى مُعارِضِها * ردَّ الغَيُورِ يدَ الجاني عنِ الحُرَمِ ثانيهما: أنه نُقلَ عنه - عليه الصلاةُ والسلام - مِنْ خوارق العاداتِ ما بَلَغَ القدْرَ الشتركَ مِنْ حَدِّ التَّواتُرِ، وإِنْ كانَ تفاصيلها آحادًا، كتسبيح الحصى في كَفَّه، وتكليم الجمادات والحيوانات، ونبع الماء من الأصابع، وظُهورِ البَرَكَةِ في الأطعمة والأشربة، وغير ذلك ما لا يُحصى كثرةً. هذا مع ما كان عليه مِنْ حُسْنِ الخُلُقِ، الذي لا يراهُ أَحَدٌ إلا ويَقْطَعُ أنه لَيسَ بكَذَّابٍ، وَإِنْ كان يَقَعُ مِنَ الصَّالِينَ العِنَادُ. وو ومنْ كمالِ خُلُقِه تمامُ الحِلْمِ والعِلْمِ مَعَ كَونِهِ وُلِدَ فِي قَوم لا يعرفون شَيْئًا، مِنْ غَير أن يتعاطى أسبابَ العِلْمِ، ووُفورِ القوة معَ قِلَّةِ أكْلِه جِدًّا، فيقْدِمُ حَيثُ تُحجَمُ الأبطال، ويقِفُ حَيثُ يفِرُّ عِندَ شِدّةِ الهَولِ صناديدُ (۱) الرّجالِ، ويثبت على حالِهِ مِنَ الدعوى لدى شدائد الأهوالِ، حتى لم يجد أعداؤه إليه مطعنا في حالٍ مِنَ الأحوالِ، بلْ شَهِدَ له العَدُوُّ والحبيب بوفورِ الكَمالِ والإِفْضال. كل ذلك نُقل إلينا بالتّواتر، فعلمنا ذلك علا ضروريًا، فلا يُعاندُ في ذلك إلا مَن اسْتَحَقَّ مِنَ اللهِ تعالى شديدَ النَّكال . وأما نُبُوهُ غَيْرِه كآدمَ فَمَنْ بَعْدَه، فَقَدْ عُلِمَ بالكتاب والسُّنّة، وأثنى عليهم الله تعالى في كِتَابِهِ بِقَولِه وَرُسُلاً مُّبَشِّرِينَ وَمُنذِرِينَ (٢) وغَيرِ ذلكَ، فَيَجِبُ لهم ما يجب له عليه ﴾ الصلاة والسلام، والبعضُ قد عيَّنَه الكتاب والبعضُ لم يُعَيَّنه. وقد ثبت بالكِتابِ والسنة أنه آخِرُ النَّبيِّينَ، فلا تُبتَدَأُ نُبوّةٌ بَعدَه عليه الصلاةُ والسلام. (1) جمع صنديد» وهو الفارس الشجاع الباسل الذي لا يقدر على دفعه أحد. (۲) سورة النساء: من الآية ١٦٥
How excellent is the saying of Sharaf ad-Din al-Busiri in al-Burda: The second section: Prophethood. Its eloquence refuted the claim of its opponent, as the jealous one repels the hand of the aggressor from the sanctities. Second: That there was transmitted from him (peace and blessings be upon him) from miraculous occurrences that reached the common level of tawatur (mass transmission), even if their details are ahad (singular reports), such as the glorification of pebbles in his palm, the speech of inanimate objects and animals, the gushing of water from his fingers, the appearance of blessing in foods and drinks, and other things beyond count. This is along with what he had of good character, which no one sees but concludes that he is not a liar, even if obstinacy occurs from the pious. And from the perfection of his character is complete forbearance and knowledge despite being born among a people who knew nothing, without engaging in the means of knowledge, and abundance of strength with very little eating, such that he advances where heroes shrink, and stands where the champions of men flee in times of great terror, and he remained firm in his claim amidst severe terrors, until his enemies found no flaw in him in any state, rather both enemy and friend testified to abundance of perfection and bounty. All of that was transmitted to us by tawatur, so we know it by necessary knowledge. None opposes this except one who deserves from Allah Almighty severe punishment. As for the prophethood of others like Adam and those after him, it is known by the Book and Sunnah, and Allah praised them in His Book saying: 'And messengers as bearers of good tidings and warners' and other verses. So what is obligatory for him (peace and blessings) is obligatory for them. Some are specified by the Book and some are not. And it is established by the Book and Sunnah that he is the seal of the prophets, so no prophethood is initiated after him (peace and blessings). (1) Plural of ṣundīd, meaning the brave, courageous horseman whom no one can repel. (2) Surah an-Nisa: verse 165.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a proof of Muhammad's prophethood. The author begins by citing a line from al-Busiri's Burda, then enumerates the miraculous events (خوارق العادات) that were transmitted from the Prophet with widespread transmission (تواتر), even if their details are singular. These miracles include: pebbles glorifying, speech of objects, water from fingers, blessing in food. Then he adds the evidence from his perfect character, which leads anyone who sees him to know he is not a liar. The description of his character includes forbearance, knowledge despite being unlettered, strength despite little food, courage in battle, and steadfastness. This character, along with the miracles, was transmitted by tawatur, producing necessary knowledge (علم ضروري). Then he contrasts the knowledge of Muhammad's prophethood with that of other prophets, which is known from scripture, not necessarily by tawatur. He also confirms that Muhammad is the seal of the prophets.

Key Terms
خوارق العادات
تواتر
آحاد
علم ضروري
حسن الخلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Muhammad's prophethood is based on weak or isolated reports.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that although some details are ahad, the overall proof from miracles and character is mutawatir (mass transmitted) and yields certain knowledge.

Checkpoint
What is the epistemological status of the knowledge of Muhammad's prophethood according to this passage?
A) Speculative (zanni)
B) Necessary (daruri)
C) Probable (ghalib al-zann)
D) Blind faith (taqlid)

Key Takeaway
Muhammad's prophethood is proven by overwhelming evidence: miraculous events and perfect character, transmitted by mass testimony producing certain knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to see the Prophet's character today, would you be convinced of his truthfulness, or would you be among those who oppose him out of arrogance? What is preventing you from fully embodying his character in your own life?
?
The passage says the Prophet's knowledge came without the means of learning. Do you rely on your own intellect and education more than on divine guidance? How can you submit your knowledge to the Prophet's teachings starting today?
?
The miracles were transmitted by many witnesses. Do you truly believe in these events as certain knowledge, or do you doubt them internally? What step will you take today to strengthen your certainty in the Prophet?

The Prophethood of Other Messengers and the Seal of Prophethood
A comparison of epistemological bases for prophethood and a declaration of finality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophethood of other messengers is known through scripture and why Muhammad is the final prophet.

Core Idea
Other prophets are known by revelation; Muhammad is the seal, no prophet after him.

After establishing the certainty of Muhammad's prophethood through direct transmission, Imam Dardeer addresses the status of other prophets. Their prophethood is known through the Book and Sunnah, not through independent tawatur. He also affirms the finality of Muhammad's prophethood, citing the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on other prophets
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author shifts from the specific proof for Muhammad to a general statement about all prophets.
The passage begins with 'As for the prophethood of others like Adam...'
2
Identify the source of knowledge for other prophets
The author states that their prophethood is known by the Book (Quran) and Sunnah, not by tawatur of miracles. He cites a verse from the Quran as proof.
Quran 4:165 mentions messengers as bearers of good tidings and warners.
3
Understand the obligation regarding other prophets
The author says that what is obligatory for Muhammad is also obligatory for other prophets (belief in their prophethood, etc.). Some are named in scripture, some are not.
This emphasizes the unity of prophethood.
4
Affirm the finality of Muhammad's prophethood
The passage ends by stating that Muhammad is the seal of the prophets, so no new prophethood is initiated after him. This is a core Islamic belief.
The Arabic uses 'آخِرُ النَّبيِّينَ' (last of the prophets).

?

?

?
If you claim that Muhammad is the seal, then every spiritual leader you follow must be subordinate to him. Are there any teachers, sheikhs, or influencers in your life whom you might be treating as a source of new guidance rather than as a mere explainer of the final message? How will you realign your heart?

The King's Analogy: How Miracles Produce Certain Knowledge
Imam Dardeer gives an analogy to explain how miracles indicate truthfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the analogy of a king's unusual action demonstrates that miracles produce necessary knowledge (علم ضروري) of a prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
Miracles produce necessary knowledge, not just probability.

Imam Dardeer presents a vivid analogy to explain why miracles compel belief in a prophet's truthfulness. In this lesson, you will see how an observable, extraordinary act confirms a claim as directly as a king's response confirms a messenger. This analogy lays the rational foundation for why Muslims hold that miracles produce certain knowledge, whether witnessed or reported through tawatur.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on the story of the king and the claimant. Let the narrative sink in before analyzing.
Notice the emphasis on the king hearing the claimant and deliberately changing his habit.
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the roles: the claimant (prophet), the king (God), the audience (people), and the extraordinary act (miracle). Understand how each part corresponds to the prophethood proof.
The king's act is a direct response to the claimant's request, not random.
3
Connect to the miracle proof
Reflect on why the audience obtains necessary knowledge (علم ضروري) from the king's act. Then see how this parallels a prophet's miracle and why the knowledge is certain.
The passage also states that this knowledge is gained even through tawatur, not just direct observation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ضَرَبَ الأشياخُ لصِدْقِ مُدّعي الرسالة بدليل المعجزة مثالًا يَتَّضِحُ به دلالتها على صدقه، ويُعلَمُ ذلك بالضرورة، فقالوا: مِثال ذلك ما إذا قامَ رَجُلٌ في مجلس ملك بحضور جماعة، وادعى أنه رسول هذا الملك إليهم، فطلبوا منه الحجة على ذلك فقال: دليلى على صدق قولي أنْ يُغيّر الملك عادته، بأنْ يقومَ عَنْ سريره، ويقعُدَ ثلاث مرات، والملك يسمع ذلك، ففعل الملكُ ذلك، فلا شكٍّ أنه يحصل للجماعةِ العِلمُ الضروري أنه صادقٌ في دعواه، ومُنَزِّلُ منزِلَةَ قَولِه صدَقَ هذا الرجُلُ فيها ادعاه» ولا فَرقَ في حُصولِ العِلم بذلك لَنْ شاهَدَه أو لم يُشاهده، ولكنْ نُقِلَ إليه خَبَرُ هذا الفعل بالتّواتُر.
The elders gave an example for the truthfulness of the claimant of messengership by the evidence of the miracle, through which its indication of his truthfulness becomes clear, and that is known necessarily. They said: An example of that is when a man stands in a king's assembly in the presence of a group, and claims that he is the messenger of this king to them. They ask him for the proof of that, so he says: 'My proof for the truth of my statement is that the king changes his custom by rising from his throne and sitting down three times, while the king hears that.' Then the king does that. There is no doubt that the group obtains necessary knowledge that he is truthful in his claim, and it is treated as if the king said, 'This man is truthful in what he claimed.' There is no difference in obtaining that knowledge whether one witnessed it or did not witness it, but rather the report of this action was conveyed to him through tawatur.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is an analogy to explain how miracles indicate the truthfulness of a prophet. The author states that the scholars (الأشياخ) gave an example: if a man in a king's assembly claims to be the king's messenger, and the king performs an unusual act (changing his habit by standing and sitting three times) in response to that claim, the audience will necessarily know that the man is truthful. This is because the king's action confirms the claimant's statement. Similarly, when a prophet claims prophethood and performs a miracle, people necessarily know he is truthful. The knowledge is obtained whether one witnesses the miracle directly or hears about it through widespread transmission (tawatur). So the analogy clarifies that miracles produce necessary knowledge (علم ضروري) of the prophet's truthfulness.

Key Terms
معجزة
علم ضروري
تواتر
صدق
رسالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles only provide probable (ظني) knowledge of a prophet's truthfulness.
Correction: The analogy shows that miracles produce necessary knowledge (علم ضروري) as certain as directly seeing the king confirm the claimant. The audience's knowledge is immediate and indubitable.

Checkpoint
According to the example, what causes the audience to necessarily know the claimant is truthful?
A) The king's statement
B) The king's unusual act in response
C) The claimant's eloquence
D) The presence of many witnesses

Key Takeaway
Miracles produce necessary knowledge of a prophet's truthfulness, just as a king's extraordinary act confirms a messenger's claim.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about the miracles of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), do you feel a deep, unshakable certainty that he was truly sent by God? If not, what is blocking that certainty in your heart?
?
The king's analogy shows that a public, witnessed miracle forces people to accept the messenger's truthfulness. If you had been present at one of the Prophet's miracles, would you have submitted immediately? What does your hesitation say about your current faith?
?
The passage says that knowledge is obtained even without direct witness, through tawatur. Are you treating the transmitted accounts of the Prophet's miracles with the same certainty as if you had seen them? If not, what change must you make in your approach to the sunna and seera?

The Obligation of Tabligh for Prophets
Imam Dardeer defines tabligh and proves its obligation from the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of tabligh (delivery) for prophets and the Quranic proof that it is an obligatory duty.

Core Idea
Tabligh is not optional; it is the essential duty of every prophet.

Imam Dardeer begins by defining what tabligh means for prophets: the conveying of divine rulings. He then grounds this definition in a powerful Quranic command that makes delivery an obligation. This passage sets the foundation for understanding prophethood and the weight of the prophetic mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of Tabligh
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on the opening definition: tabligh is conveying the rulings to the people.
Notice the phrase 'إيصال الأحكام'.
2
Analyze the Quranic proof
The author cites Quran 5:67. See how the command 'بَلِّغْ' and the warning about failing to convey prove obligation.
The command indicates obligation in Islamic legal theory.
3
Reflect on the implications
The passage extends this obligation to all prophets and links it to their roles as bearers of glad tidings and warners.
Reflect on the severity: not delivering even part is like delivering nothing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتبليغ) أي: إيصال الأحكام التي أُمِرُوا بتبليغها إلى المرسل إليهم، إذْ التبليغ مأمورونَ بالتبليغ، قال تعالى: ﴿يَأَيُّهَا الرَّسُولُ بَلِّغْ مَا أُنزِلَ إِلَيْكَ مِن رَّبَّكَ وَإِن لَّمْ تَفْعَلْ فَمَا بَلَّغْتَ  ِرسَالَتَهُ ) ، والأمرُ للوجوب، وقد تقَدَّمَ أنهم لا يخونون الله تعالى بفعل منهي عنه. وما ثبت له عليه الصلاة والسلام يثبتُ لهم، وقال تعالى: ﴿رُسُلاً مُّبَشِّرِينَ وَمُنذِرِينَ ﴾ () ولا يتم التبشير والإنذار إلا بالتبليغ. (۱) سورة المائدة: من الآية ٦٧ . أي: وإن لم تبلغ بعض ما أمرت بتبليغه من الرسالة فحكمك حكم من لم يبلغ شيئا منها. فانظر هذا التخويف العظيم لأشرف خلقه وأكملهم معرفة به، فكان خوفه على قدر معرفته، وقد شهد الله تعالى له بكمال التبليغ في قوله: (الْيَوْمَ أَكْمَلْتُ لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ وَأَتْمَمْتُ عَلَيْكُمْ نِعْمَتِي .. ) الآية [المائدة: ٣]. [سباعی، ص ٤٣٣ بتصرف]
(At-Tabligh) i.e., conveying the rulings that they were commanded to deliver to those to whom they were sent, since they are commanded to deliver. Allah said: 'O Messenger, convey what has been revealed to you from your Lord, and if you do not, then you have not conveyed His message.' And the command is for obligation. It has preceded that they do not betray Allah by doing a forbidden act. And what is established for him (peace and blessings) is established for them. And Allah said: 'Messengers as bearers of good tidings and warners.' And the bearing of good tidings and warning is not complete except through delivery. (1) Surah al-Ma'idah: verse 67. Meaning: If you do not convey some of what you were commanded to convey of the message, then your judgment is that of one who did not convey any of it. Look at this great intimidation for the noblest of His creation and the most complete in knowledge of Him, for his fear was in proportion to his knowledge. Allah testified to the completeness of his delivery in His saying: 'Today I have completed for you your religion and perfected upon you My favor...' al-Ma'idah: 3. [Subai'i, p. 433, adapted]
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage defines التبليغ (delivery) as the communication of the rulings that prophets are commanded to convey to their people. The author proves its obligation using the Quranic verse from Surah al-Ma'idah, where Allah commands the Prophet to deliver what was revealed, and warns that failure to do so would mean he has not conveyed the message at all. Since the command indicates obligation, and since prophets do not disobey Allah, they must deliver. The author also notes that what is established for Muhammad (صلى الله عليه وسلم) is also established for other prophets. Then he cites another verse that describes prophets as bearers of good news and warners, arguing that these roles cannot be fulfilled without delivery. The footnote elaborates on the verse, emphasizing the gravity of the command and the completeness of the Prophet's delivery.

The Necessity of Fatanah for Prophets
Imam Dardeer defines fatanah and states its necessity for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets must possess exceptional intelligence (fatanah) and what qualities are incompatible with prophethood.

Core Idea
Prophets must be the most intelligent to establish proofs and refute doubts.

Imam Dardeer explains that a key attribute of prophets is extraordinary intelligence. Without it, they could not effectively argue against falsehood and establish divine proofs. This lesson examines the definition of fatanah and its necessity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to get the overall meaning.
Notice the straightforward structure: definition, prohibition, reason.
2
Identify the definition of fatanah
Find how Imam Dardeer defines fatanah (حدة العقل وذكاؤه). This is the foundation.
Fatanah is sharpness of mind and intelligence.
3
Note the three prohibited traits
The passage states that a prophet cannot be mughaffal, ablah, or balid. Understand each term.
The footnotes clarify their meanings.
4
Understand the reasoning
Why are these traits prohibited? Because prophets are sent to establish proofs and refute doubts.
This requires high intelligence.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider why intelligence is an essential attribute of prophethood, not a secondary one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفطانة) بفتح الفاء، وهي حِدَةُ العقل وذَكاؤه)، فلا يجوز أنْ يكونَ الرسول ولا الفطانة النبي مُغَفَّلًا أو أبْلَه أو بليدا(۳)، لأنهم أرسلوا لإقامةِ الحَجَج وإبْطالِ شُبَهِ المجادلين، (۲) المراد بها التفطن والتيقظ لإلزام الخصوم وإحجاجهم، وطرق إبطال دعاويهم الباطلة، والتفطن والذكاء: إدراك الأمور الدقيقة، وهو أخص من الفهم. [سباعي، ص ٤٣٥] (۳) المغفل هو الذي تدخل عليه الأمور الخفية كالشبه المزخرفة، لكن إذا نبهته تنبه، وأما البليد فهو الذي لا يفهم المسألة إلا بعسر، والأبله مرادف للمغفل . [ سباعي، ص ٤٣٦]
(Al-Faṭānah) with fath on the fa, and it is sharpness of mind and intelligence. So it is not permissible for the messenger or the prophet to be heedless, foolish, or dull, because they were sent to establish proofs and refute the doubts of disputants. (2) By it is meant attentiveness and vigilance to compel opponents and argue against them, and methods of refuting their false claims. Attentiveness and intelligence: perception of subtle matters, which is more specific than understanding. [Subai'i, p. 435] (3) Al-mughaffal is the one into whom hidden matters like embellished doubts enter, but if you alert him, he becomes alert. As for al-balīd, he is the one who does not understand the matter except with difficulty. Al-ablah is synonymous with al-mughaffal. [Subai'i, p. 436]
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage defines الفطانة (intelligence) as sharpness of mind and quickness of understanding. The author then states that it is not permissible for a prophet or messenger to be مُغَفَّل (heedless), أَبْلَه (foolish), or بَلِيد (dull). The reason is that prophets are sent to establish proofs (إقامة الحجج) and refute the doubts (شبه) of those who argue against them. This requires high intelligence. The footnotes clarify the meanings: al-mughaffal is someone susceptible to subtle false arguments but can be alerted; al-balīd has difficulty understanding; al-ablah is synonymous with al-mughaffal. Thus, prophets must possess superior intellect to effectively counter opposition.

The Obligation of Tablīgh (Delivery of the Message)
Defining tablīgh and proving its obligation with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that tablīgh (conveying the divine message) is an obligatory attribute of prophets, supported by Quranic commands.

Core Idea
Prophets must deliver the message; it is not optional.

Prophethood is not merely a title; it comes with a duty. The prophets were sent to convey God's rulings to humanity. In this lesson, we examine the definition of tablīgh and the Quranic evidence that makes it an obligation, not a recommendation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. This will give you the overall meaning of the definition and the proofs.
Pay attention to the imperative verb used in the Quranic verse.
2
Identify the two Quranic proofs
The passage cites two verses. Identify each and see how they support the obligation of tablīgh.
The first verse commands delivery; the second implies it through the role of messengers.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this attribute is important. Without tablīgh, the purpose of prophethood would be unfulfilled.
This connects to the broader understanding of prophethood in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والتبليغ) أي: إيصال الأحكام التي أُمِرُوا بتبليغها إلى المرسل إليهم، إذْ التبليغ مأمورونَ بالتبليغ، قال تعالى: ﴿يَأَيُّهَا الرَّسُولُ بَلِّغْ مَا أُنزِلَ إِلَيْكَ مِن رَّبَّكَ وَإِن لَّمْ تَفْعَلْ فَمَا بَلَّغْتَ  ِرسَالَتَهُ ) ، والأمرُ للوجوب، وقد تقَدَّمَ أنهم لا يخونون الله تعالى بفعل منهي عنه. وما ثبت له عليه الصلاة والسلام يثبتُ لهم، وقال تعالى: ﴿رُسُلاً مُّبَشِّرِينَ وَمُنذِرِينَ ﴾ () ولا يتم التبشير والإنذار إلا بالتبليغ.
(And tablīgh) i.e., delivering the rulings that they were commanded to convey to those to whom they were sent. For they are commanded to convey. Commentary

The passage notes that prophets are free from betrayal (khiyānah), so they must fulfill this duty. It also cites the verse about messengers being bearers of good news and warners, implying that this role requires delivering the message. Thus, tablīgh is an obligatory attribute of prophets.

Prophets Must Possess Fatanah (Sharp Intelligence)
Sanusi defines fatanah and provides three proofs that prophets must possess it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets must possess sharp intelligence (fatanah) and be free from heedlessness, simple-mindedness, and dullness.

Core Idea
Prophets need sharp minds to prove truth and be perfect examples.

Sanusi explains that prophets must have intellect sharp enough to establish proofs against opponents and to be followed by believers. He defines fatanah and gives three reasons why dullness is incompatible with prophethood. This lesson unpacks those reasons and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to get a sense of the argument Sanusi presents.
2
Identify the three reasons
Look for the three distinct reasons Sanusi gives why prophets cannot be heedless, simple-minded, or dull. Notice how each reason builds on the role of the prophet.
The reasons are introduced by 'because' (لأن) or 'and because' (ولأن).
3
Reflect on lineage and murū'ah
Consider the final part of the passage where Sanusi links fatanah to noble lineage and moral conduct. Ask yourself why these are necessary for prophets.
This connects to the idea that prophets are perfect examples in all aspects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والفطانة) بفتح الفاء، وهي حِدَةُ العقل وذَكاؤه)، فلا يجوز أنْ يكونَ الرسول ولا الفطانة النبي مُغَفَّلًا أو أبْلَه أو بليدا(۳)، لأنهم أرسلوا لإقامةِ الحَجَج وإبْطالِ شُبَهِ المجادلين، ولا يكون ذلك مِنْ مُغَفَّل ولا أبْلَه، ولأنا مأمورونَ بالاقتداء بهم في الأقوال والأفعال، والمقتدى به لا يكون بليدا، ولأنَّ البلادة صفةُ نقص تُحِلُّ بِمَنْصِبهم الشريف. ومن ذلك يُعْلَمُ أنهم لا يكونونَ إِلا مِنْ أَشْرَفِ الناسِ، رِجالا ونساءً، إِذْ شأنُ دَنيء الأُصولِ أنْ تأْنَفَ النَّفْسُ مِنَ اتَّبَاعِه والاقتداء به. العليّةِ عليهم صلَواتُ الله وسلامه . ولذا كانوا مُنَزَّهِينَ عَنْ كُلِّ ما يُخل بالمروءة، وكُل ما يؤدّي إلى نقص في مراتبهم
(And al-faṭānah) with fatha on the fa, and it is sharpness of intellect and intelligence. So it is not permissible that the messenger—nor the prophet—be heedless (mghaffal) or simple-minded (ablah) or dull (balīd), because they were sent to establish proofs and invalidate the doubts of disputants. And that cannot be from one who is heedless or simple-minded. Also because we are commanded to follow them in words and actions, and the one followed cannot be dull. And because dullness is an attribute of deficiency unbefitting their noble station. From that it is known that they are only from the noblest of people, men and women, for the nature of one of low origin is that the soul dislikes following him and taking him as an example. (This is due to) their high station, prayers and peace of Allah be upon them. And therefore they are free from everything that violates chivalry (murū'ah) and everything that leads to deficiency in their ranks.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage defines faṭānah as sharpness of intellect and intelligence. It then states the ruling: it is impermissible for a prophet to be heedless (mghaffal), simple-minded (ablah), or dull (balīd). Three reasons are given: First, prophets were sent to establish proofs and refute the doubts of opponents, which requires sharp intellect. Second, believers are commanded to follow the prophets in all sayings and actions, and a dull person cannot be a proper example. Third, dullness is a defect unbecoming of the prophets’ lofty rank. The passage concludes that prophets must be from the noblest lineage, as people naturally disdain following those of low origin. Their high station demands that they be free from anything that violates proper conduct (murū'ah) or diminishes their status.

Impossible Attributes: Khianah and Prophetic Actions
Explaining the impossibility of khianah and the nature of prophetic acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that betrayal (khianah) is impossible for prophets and that their actions, even permissible ones, are accompanied by a noble intention such as teaching.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from betrayal and even permissible acts are elevated by intention.

Having established the wajibat (obligatory attributes) for prophets, Sanusi now turns to their opposites, which are impossible. This lesson focuses on the first impossible attribute, khianah (betrayal), and clarifies that prophets never commit prohibited acts. Moreover, even their permissible actions are never mundane; they are always performed with a higher intention, such as teaching the community.

Guided Path
1
Read the poetic line and its commentary
Start by reading the Arabic poetic line (bayt) and its translation. Notice that it states the opposites of the wajibat are impossible, while permissible acts like eating are possible for prophets.
The poem is a compact summary; the commentary expands it.
2
Understand the meaning of khianah
Identify what khianah means: doing a prohibited act. The passage says it is impossible for prophets. Consider why this is essential for their role as trustworthy messengers.
3
Distinguish between two perspectives on actions
The passage makes a key distinction: looking at actions in themselves (fi haddhi dhatihi) versus considering accidental circumstances (bi hasabi 'awaridih). Under the first view, acts can be wajib, mandub, or mubah. Under the second, prophets only do wajib or mandub.
This distinction resolves how prophets can appear to do permissible acts without lowering their rank.
4
Learn how permissible acts occur from prophets
When prophets do a permissible act, it is always accompanied by an intention (niyyah) that makes it sought after (matlub). The least of such intentions is legislating for others (tashri'), which is a form of teaching. Reflect on the high rank this implies.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you grasped the central point: permissible acts from prophets are accompanied by an intention that transforms them.
The answer is found directly in the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٥١ - ويستحيلُ ضِدُّها عليهِمُ * وجائز كالأكل في حقهِمُ (ويستحيلُ) في حقهم عليهم السلام ( ضِدُّها) أَيْ: ضِدُّ هذه الواجباتِ الأربعةِ التَقَدِّمة) (عليهم) فيمْتَنعُ في حقهم: - الخيانة بفعل مَنْهيَّ عنه؛ إذ أفعاهم لا تخلو عن الواجِبِ والمندوب والمباحِ، وهذا بالنَّظر إلى الفعل في حَدِّ ذاته. وأما لو نُظِرَ إليه بحَسَب عوارِضِه فالحقُّ أنَّ أفعالهم دائرةٌ بَينَ الواجب والمندوبِ لا غير، وأما المباحُ فلا يَقَعُ منهم كما يقعُ مِنْ غَيْرِهم، بل لا يَقَعُ مِنهُم إِلا مُصاحِبًا لنيَةٍ تضْرِفُه إلى كَونِه مطلوبًا، وأقله قصْدُ التشريع للغير، وذلك مِنْ بابِ التعليم، وناهيك به مرتبةٌ.
51. And their opposite is impossible for them * and permissible like eating in their regard. (And it is impossible) in their right, peace be upon them, (their opposite) i.e., the opposite of these four preceding obligatory attributes (for them). So it is impossible in their right: betrayal (al-khiyānah) by doing a prohibited act. For their actions are not devoid of the obligatory, the recommended, and the permissible – this is with regard to the action in itself. But if it is considered according to its accidental circumstances, the truth is that their actions circulate only between the obligatory and the recommended. As for the permissible, it does not occur from them as it occurs from others. Rather, it occurs from them only accompanied by an intention that turns it into something sought after, the least of which is the intention of legislating for others. And that is from the category of teaching. And how excellent a rank it is!
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage begins with a poetic line stating that the opposites of the four wajibat are impossible for prophets, while permissible acts like eating are possible. The commentary then explains: the impossible opposites include betrayal (khiyānah), which is doing a prohibited act. The passage clarifies the nature of prophets' actions. When considering actions in themselves (fī ḥaddhi dhātihi), prophets' actions may be obligatory, recommended, or permissible. However, when considering actions according to their accidental circumstances (bi-ḥasabi ʿawāriḍihi), their actions are only either obligatory or recommended. Permissible actions do not occur from them as they occur from others. Rather, if a permissible action occurs, it is accompanied by an intention that makes it sought after, such as the intention of legislating (tashrīʿ) for others, which falls under teaching (taʿlīm). This emphasizes the high rank of prophets.

Correction: Prophets are protected from all sins (including khianah). Even their permissible acts are done with an intention that raises them to recommended acts, such as the intention of teaching (tashri').

Prophets are immune from betrayal and even their permissible acts are elevated by a noble intention, teaching us the high standard of prophetic conduct.

?

?
If betrayal (khianah) is impossible for prophets because they never choose a prohibited act, why do you sometimes allow yourself to slip into minor sins? What does your standard of action say about your care for your own prophethood-following?

Prophets are from the Noblest and Not Dull
Establishes that prophets are from the noblest people and not dull.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets must be from the noblest lineage and free from dullness, based on the rational argument that followers would not accept a dull leader.

Core Idea
Prophets must be noble and intelligent because we are commanded to follow them.

This passage from Imam Dardir establishes an important rational basis for the conditions of prophethood. Before discussing prophetic miracles or infallibility, we must recognize that prophets are chosen from the best of humanity. The argument here is straightforward: since we are required to follow them in word and deed, they cannot be dull or of lowly origin, as that would defeat the purpose of their leadership.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the key terms: مغفل (heedless), أبله (dullard), بلادة (dullness), مروءة (decency).
2
Identify the two reasons
The passage gives two reasons why prophets cannot be dull. First, because we are commanded to follow them, and a dull person cannot be followed. Second, because dullness is a deficiency that degrades their noble station.
3
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that prophets are only from the noblest people, both men and women, and are free from anything that violates decency.
4
Reflect on the significance
This shows that lineage and intelligence are prerequisites for prophethood, not just piety. It counters the misconception that prophets could be of lowly birth or unintelligent.

Source Text

The highness upon them, prayers of Allah and peace. And therefore they are purified from everything that violates decency, and everything that leads to deficiency in their ranks.

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the section on prophethood. It argues that prophets must be from the noblest lineage and free from mental dullness. The reasoning is: We are commanded to follow them in words and deeds, and a follower would not accept a dull leader. Also, dullness is a deficiency that contradicts their high rank. Therefore, prophets are only from the most noble families, both male and female, because low-born individuals would not be followed willingly. The passage concludes that prophets are free from anything that violates decency or leads to deficiency.

Four Impossible Attributes and the Proof of No Betrayal
Classifies the four impossibles and proves betrayal impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four attributes that are impossible for prophets and the detailed proof that betrayal cannot occur due to the nature of their actions.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from four opposites; their acts are never mere mubah, so betrayal is impossible.

This lesson builds on the four obligatory attributes of prophets by exploring their opposites—the attributes that can never be true of a prophet. The author focuses especially on proving that betrayal (khiana) is impossible, based on the principle that prophetic actions always serve a higher purpose. Through this analysis, we deepen our appreciation of prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic and translation to get the overall argument structure. Notice how the poem line introduces the topic.
2
Identify the four impossible attributes
From the footnote (indicated by '1'), find the four opposites: betrayal (خيانة), lying (كذب), concealment (كتمان), and dullness (بلادة). Write them down.
3
Understand the proof for betrayal
Analyze how the author proves betrayal impossible. He classifies all prophetic actions as either obligatory, recommended, or permissible with an intention. No action is purely prohibited.
The key point is that even permissible acts are accompanied by an intention like teaching the community.
4
Reflect on the saint analogy
The author compares prophets to saints who elevate permissible acts through good intentions. Realize that prophets are even more elevated, so betrayal is far from them.

(ويستحيلُ) في حقهم عليهم السلام ( ضِدُّها) أَيْ: ضِدُّ هذه الواجباتِ الأربعةِ التَقَدِّمة) (عليهم) فيمْتَنعُ في حقهم:

وأما لو نُظِرَ إليه بحسَب عوارِضِه فالحقُّ أنَّ أفعالهم دائرةٌ بَينَ الواجب والمندوبِ لا غير، وأما المباحُ فلا يَقَعُ منهم كما يقعُ مِنْ غَيْرِهم، بل لا يَقَعُ مِنهُم إِلا مُصاحِبًا لنيَةٍ تضْرِفُه إلى كَونِه مطلوبًا، وأقله قصْدُ التشريع للغير، وذلك مِنْ بابِ التعليم، وناهيك به مرتبةً.
(1) المراد بالضد مطلق المنافي، وذلك لأن الكذب عدم مطابقة الخبر للواقع والخيانة فعل المحرمات والمكروهات، والكتمان عدم الوفاء بما أمروا بتبليغه للخلق، وحينئذ فالتقابل بين الصدق والكذب تقابل الشيء والمساوي لنقيضه، وأما بين الأمانة والخيانة فتقابل الضدين لأنه فسر الخيانة بالفعل وهو وجودي، وأما بين التبليغ والكتمان فتقابل الشيء والمساوي لنقيضه، وكذا بين الفطانة والبلادة. 51 - And its opposite is impossible for them, and permissible like eating in their case. (And it is impossible) in their case, peace be upon them, (its opposite) i.e., the opposite of these four obligatory attributes (mentioned earlier) (upon them). So it is impossible in their case: - Betrayal by doing a prohibited act; because their actions are not free from the obligatory, the recommended, and the permissible, and this is considering the action in itself. But if it is considered according to its accidents, the truth is that their actions are confined between the obligatory and the recommended only. As for the permissible, it does not occur from them as it occurs from others. Rather, it only occurs from them accompanied by an intention that diverts it to being sought, the least of which is the intention of legislation for others, and that is from the category of teaching, and sufficient is it as a rank. (1) By opposite is meant absolute contrary, because lying is the non-conformity of the report to reality, and betrayal is the commission of prohibitions and disliked acts, and concealment is failure to fulfill what they were commanded to convey to creation, and then the opposition between truthfulness and lying is the opposition of thing and equal to its contrary, and between trustworthiness and betrayal is the opposition of contraries because betrayal is interpreted as an act which is existent, and between conveying and concealing is the opposition of thing and equal to its contrary, and likewise between intelligence and dullness. [Hashiyat al-Sawi, p. 61] And if some of their followers, like the saints, their actions are not free from the obligatory and the recommended by diverting permissible things with good intention to recommended acts, such as diverting eating for strength for worship and building the body, and intercourse for protecting the soul from the forbidden and for the desired offspring and other than that, then how about these noble masters, upon them the best prayer and peace.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage classifies the four impossible attributes for prophets—betrayal, lying, concealment, and dullness—and provides a detailed proof for the impossibility of betrayal. The author begins by quoting a poem that states the opposite of the four wajibat is impossible for prophets. The commentary explains that the opposites are the four: betrayal, lying, concealment, and dullness. Betrayal is impossible because prophets' actions are never pure acts of disobedience. Considering their actions in themselves, they are not free from the three categories: obligatory, recommended, permissible. But considering the intentions, their actions are always obligatory or recommended; even permissible acts are accompanied by an intention that elevates them, such as teaching by example. A footnote clarifies the precise logical relationship between each attribute and its opposite. The author then reinforces this by noting that even saintly followers transform permissible acts into recommended ones through intention, so prophets are even more elevated.
