The Impossible Crime: Why Prophets Never Lie
Al-Dardir proves prophetic infallibility using a Quranic conditional argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitive Quranic proof that prophets cannot lie in conveying revelation, and how this establishes their trustworthiness.

Core Idea
The Quran itself threatens the Prophet with death if he lied — proving his utter trustworthiness.

We have already learned that prophets are protected from sin and error. Now we consider: could a prophet ever lie about Allah? Imam al-Dardir presents a two-part proof: a logical argument and a direct Quranic threat. This lesson focuses on the second, most powerful proof — the verse that promises destruction if the Prophet ever fabricated a lie.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the Quranic verse and the commentator's notes.
The verse is from Surah al-Haqqah (69:44-47).
2
Understand the Quranic argument
Identify the conditional: if the Prophet had fabricated sayings, then Allah would seize him and cut his aorta (kill him). The consequence (death) did not occur, so the condition (lying) is impossible.
Think of it as: If P then Q; not Q, therefore not P.
3
Reflect on the strength of the proof
Consider why this is a decisive proof: it comes from Allah Himself, and it promises immediate punishment. This shows lying is impossible not just after prophethood but at any time.
The commentator clarifies 'seizing by the right hand' means destruction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
- وكذا يستحيلُ عليهم الكَذِبُ؛ لما مَرَّ (۱)، ولقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَوْ تَقَوَّلَ عَلَيْنَا بَعْضَ الأَقَاوِيل * لأَخَذْنَا مِنْهُ بِالْيَمِينِ * ثُمَّ لَقَطَعْنَا مِنْهُ الْوَتِينَ * فَمَا مِنكُمْ مِّنْ أَحَدٍ عَنْهُ حاجزين (۳).
(۱) أي من لزوم الكذب في خبره تعالى. (۲) لأَخَذْنَا مِنْهُ بِالْيَمِين المراد منه هنا الهلاك، وقوله: ﴿ثُمَّ لَقَطَعْنَا مِنْهُ الْوَتِينَ) لازم لما قبله، لأنه يلزم من الهلاك قطع الوتين، وهو عرق بالقفا. [سباعي، ص ٤٤١] (۳) سورة الحاقة: الآيات ٤٤-٤٧
And likewise, lying is impossible for them, due to what has passed (1), and due to His statement, the Most High: 'And if he had fabricated against Us some sayings, We would have seized him by the right hand, then We would have cut from him the aorta, and none of you could have withheld [Us] from him.' (3) (1) i.e., from the necessity of lying in the report of Allah, the Most High. (2) 'We would have seized him by the right hand' intended here is destruction, and His statement: 'then We would have cut from him the aorta' is a necessary consequence of the previous, because destruction necessitates cutting the aorta, which is a vein at the back of the neck. (3) Surah Al-Haqqah: verses 44-47.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage proves that lying is impossible for prophets. The proof is twofold: first, by referencing a previous argument (that lying would imply lying in Allah's reports), and second, by a direct Quranic text. The verse from Surah al-Haqqah states that if the Prophet (ﷺ) had fabricated any saying against Allah, Allah would have seized him and cut his aorta, and no one could protect him. Since the Prophet was not destroyed, it is impossible that he ever lied about Allah. The commentator explains that 'seizing by the right hand' here means destruction, and cutting the aorta symbolizes death. This verse serves as a definitive proof of prophetic infallibility in conveying revelation.

Misconception: Some believe lying is possible for prophets before they receive prophethood, or that minor lies might be allowed for a greater good.
Correction: This verse shows that even a single fabrication against Allah would result in immediate destruction. The threat is absolute and covers all times, including before prophethood, because the Prophet is always under Allah's protection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Why Prophets Cannot Conceal: The Three Categories of Divine Transmission
Proves concealment is impossible and outlines three categories of transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets cannot conceal what they are commanded to convey, and how their knowledge is divided into three categories based on divine command.

Core Idea
Prophets obey Allah perfectly—they conceal only what He commands them to conceal.

A common question about prophethood is whether prophets ever withheld knowledge. This passage answers by first proving that concealment of obligatory revelation is impossible, then explaining that not all knowledge is meant for public dissemination. The author outlines three categories of what prophets bring, showing that selective sharing of permitted secrets is not a fault.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the Quranic proof and the subsequent classification.
The passage uses the term 'كتمان' (concealment) in two different contexts.
2
Understand the proof from the Quran
The author quotes verse 159 of Surah al-Baqarah to show that concealers are cursed. Prophets cannot fall under this curse, so they cannot conceal what they are commanded to convey.
This is a rational proof based on prophetic infallibility.
3
Identify the three categories
The passage summarizes three types: (1) commanded to convey → fully conveyed; (2) commanded to conceal → fully concealed; (3) given a choice → conveyed partially to some individuals.
The third category includes the four caliphs and Abu Hurayrah, among saints.
4
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
Reflect on how this shows that prophets are obedient in both revealing and hiding knowledge according to Allah's command.
This clarifies that concealment is not a flaw when commanded by Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
- وكذا يستحيلُ عليهم كتمانُ شَيءٍ لِما أُمِرُوا بتبليغه، إذ كيف يقعُ مِنهم الكتمان، وهو ملعون صاحبه، بنَصٌ قَولِه تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يَكْتُمُونَ مَا أَنزَلْنَا مِنَ الْبَيِّنَات وَالْهُدَى مِن بَعْدِ مَا بَيَّنَّاهُ لِلنَّاسِ فِي الْكِتَابِ (4) الآية . (٤)
وأما ما لم يؤمروا بتبليغه فبعضه يُخيَّرون في تبليغه، وهو ما لم يؤمروا بعدم تبليغه، وبعضُه يجب كتمانه، وهو ما أمروا بكتمانه (٥) ، كبعض الأسرار الإلهية، وبعضُ هذا القِسمِ أذِنَ لهم في إيصاله لبعض الأفراد، كالخلفاء الأربعة وكأبي هُرَيرةَ رَضَلَّ عَنْهُ، وهذه الأسرار هي المتداولةُ بَينَ الأولياء.
(٤) سورة البقرة: من الآية ١٥٩
(٥) الحاصل أن ما جاء به الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام على ثلاثة أقسام: ۱- قسم أمروا بتبليغه فلم يكتموا منه حرفا، ۲- قسم أمروا بكتمانه فلم يبلغوا منه حرفا، ٣- قسم خيروا بين كتمانه وتبليغه فبلغوا البعض وكتموا البعض.
And likewise, concealment of anything they were commanded to convey is impossible for them, for how can concealment occur from them, while its possessor is cursed by the text of His statement the Most High: 'Indeed, those who conceal what We sent down of clear proofs and guidance after We made it clear for the people in the Scripture...' (4) the verse. (4) Surah Al-Baqarah: from verse 159. As for that which they were not commanded to convey, some of it they are given a choice in conveying it, which is that which they were not commanded not to convey; and some of it it is obligatory to conceal it, which is that which they were commanded to conceal (5), such as some divine secrets. And some of this category they were permitted to convey to certain individuals, such as the four caliphs and Abu Hurayrah, may Allah be pleased with them, and these secrets are those circulated among the saints. (5) The summary: What the messengers brought, peace be upon them, is of three types: 1- That which they were commanded to convey, so they did not conceal a letter of it; 2- That which they were commanded to conceal, so they did not convey a letter of it; 3- That which they were given a choice between concealing and conveying, so they conveyed some and concealed some.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage proves that concealment of what prophets are commanded to convey is impossible. The primary proof is that Allah curses those who conceal divine guidance, and prophets are immune from that curse. However, not all knowledge is meant for public dissemination. The author explains three categories: (1) What prophets were commanded to convey to everyone – they conveyed it fully. (2) What they were commanded to conceal, such as certain divine secrets – they kept it hidden. (3) What they were given a choice about – they could reveal to some individuals, like the four caliphs and Abu Hurayrah, and these secrets are passed among saints. This shows that while concealment of obligatory revelation is impossible, selective sharing of permitted secrets is not a fault.

Key Terms
كتمان
تبليغ
أسرار إلهية
خلفاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that prophets cannot conceal anything at all, implying they must reveal all knowledge they possess.
Correction: The passage clarifies that prophets obey Allah's command in both revealing and concealing. They are required to conceal certain divine secrets as commanded, so concealment in those cases is not a flaw.

Checkpoint

A) They are forgiven
B) They are cursed
C) They are rewarded
D) They are praised

Key Takeaway
Prophets perfectly obey Allah: they convey what is commanded and conceal what is commanded, including divine secrets shared only with select individuals.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You see that prophets obeyed Allah perfectly in both conveying and concealing. When have you spoken or remained silent out of obedience to Allah, and when have you let fear or desire dictate your words? What would change if you treated every word as a command from Allah?
?
The passage shows that some knowledge is not for everyone. Are there truths about yourself, your faith, or your shortcomings that you conceal out of pride rather than obedience? What would it cost you to bring them into the light?
?
Prophets were entrusted with divine secrets and shared them only with those worthy. Consider your own circle: do you share sacred knowledge carelessly, or do you guard it appropriately? How can you better honor the trust Allah places in you regarding what you know?

The Impossibility of Lying for Prophets
Dardeer proves the impossibility of lying for prophets with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why lying is impossible for prophets according to Islamic theology, based on rational and Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Prophets cannot lie because Allah protects them from fabrication.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer presents a key proof for the infallibility of prophets ('isma). He argues that lying is impossible for them, both by rational necessity and by explicit Quranic threat. The verse from Surah al-Haqqah shows that if a prophet fabricated a saying, Allah would immediately punish him — and since prophets are never punished, they cannot fabricate.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully, noting the key terms 'يستحيل' (impossible) and 'الكذب' (lying). Then read the English translation.
The passage is concise; each word carries weight.
2
Identify the two proofs
The passage mentions two pieces of evidence: 'لما مر' (the rational proof from earlier) and the Quranic verse. Understand that the rational proof was already established in the previous lesson.
The verse is the main focus here.
3
Analyze the Quranic verse
Read the verse (69:44-47) and its translation. Notice the severe punishment threatened: seizure, cutting of the aorta. Ask: Why does this prove prophets cannot lie?
Because prophets are protected from such punishment, so they cannot fabricate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا يستحيل عليهم الكذب؛ لما مر، ولقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَوْ تَقَوَّلَ عَلَيْنَا بَعْضَ الْأَقَاوِيلِ * لَأَخَذْنَا مِنْهُ بِالْيَمِينِ * ثُمَّ لَقَطَعْنَا مِنْهُ الْوَتِينَ * فَمَا مِنكُم مِّنْ أَحَدٍ عَنْهُ حَاجِزِينَ﴾
Likewise, lying is impossible for them because of what has passed and due to His statement, the Exalted: 'And if he had fabricated against Us any saying, We would have seized him by the right hand, then We would have cut from him the aorta, and none of you could have held [Us] off from him.'
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the Qur'an for the impossibility of lying for prophets. It begins by stating that lying is impossible for them, referencing a previous argument (based on the necessity that if they lied, Allah's confirmation of their truthfulness would be false). Then it cites the verse from Surah al-Haqqah (69:44-47) which threatens anyone who fabricates sayings against Allah with immediate punishment, implying that since prophets are protected from punishment, they cannot fabricate. The verse is a decisive textual proof (dalil qat'i) used in kalam to establish prophetic infallibility.

Key Terms
يستحيل
الكذب
التقول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets could lie about religious matters, either deliberately or unintentionally.
Correction: The Quranic threat shows that if a prophet fabricated, Allah would punish him immediately. Since prophets are sinless and protected, they cannot lie.

Checkpoint
According to the verse cited, what would happen if a prophet fabricated a saying against Allah?
A) He would be forgiven
B) He would be seized and his aorta cut
C) He would be rebuked gently
D) He would be left alone

Key Takeaway
The Quranic threat confirms that prophets are sinless in conveying revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Allah would cut your aorta the moment you spoke falsely about Him, how would your speech about religion change starting today?
?
What falsehoods about Allah or His guidance have you silently tolerated in conversations, books, or lectures? This verse demands you reject them — will you, and what will you do about it?
?
Since Allah protects His messengers from even the possibility of lying about Him, how does that affect your certainty in the Quran as His final word? Are you willing to submit your doubts to this promise?

The Impossibility of Concealing Revelation
Dardeer proves the impossibility of prophets concealing what they must convey.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets cannot conceal any part of the revelation they are commanded to deliver, and the Quranic evidence for this.

Core Idea
Prophets cannot conceal revelation; concealing it is cursed by Allah.

Prophets are entrusted with delivering divine revelation, but could they ever hide part of it? Imam Dardeer establishes a firm principle: it is impossible for them to conceal what they are ordered to convey. He supports this with a powerful Quranic verse that condemns concealment. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how Dardeer states the impossibility as a given fact.
2
Identify the Quranic proof
Find the verse cited and understand how it supports the claim. The verse curses those who conceal clear proofs and guidance.
The verse is from Surah al-Baqarah (2:159).
3
Reflect on the rhetorical question
Dardeer asks 'how could concealment occur from them?' This emphasizes the absurdity of the idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا يستحيل عليهم كتمان شيء لما أمروا بتبليغه، إذ كيف يقع منهم الكتمان، وهو ملعون صاحبه، بنص قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يَكْتُمُونَ مَا أَنزَلْنَا مِنَ الْبَيِّنَاتِ وَالْهُدَى مِن بَعْدِ مَا بَيَّنَّاهُ لِلنَّاسِ فِي الْكِتَابِ﴾ الآية. وأما ما لم يؤمروا بتبليغه فبعضه يخيرون في تبليغه، وهو ما لم يؤمروا بعدم تبليغه، وبعضه يجب كتمانه، وهو ما أمروا بكتمانه، كبعض الأسرار الإلهية، وبعض هذا القسم أذن لهم في إيصاله لبعض الأفراد، كالخلفاء الأربعة وكأبي هريرة رضي الله عنهم، وهذه الأسرار هي المتداولة بين الأولياء.
Likewise, concealing anything they were commanded to convey is impossible for them, for how could concealment occur from them when its possessor is cursed, according to the text of His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, those who conceal what We sent down of clear proofs and guidance after We made it clear for the people in the Scripture' – the verse. As for what they were not commanded to convey, some of it they are given the choice in conveying – that which they were not commanded not to convey; and some of it they must conceal – that which they were commanded to conceal, such as some divine secrets; and some of this category they were permitted to convey to certain individuals, such as the four caliphs and Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with them, and these secrets are those circulated among the saints.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a twofold teaching: first, it proves that prophets cannot conceal any part of the revelation they are ordered to deliver, citing the verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:159) that curses those who conceal clear proofs and guidance. Second, it classifies what they were not commanded to convey into three types: (1) that which they were given choice to convey or not, which is neither commanded to convey nor to conceal; (2) that which they must conceal, such as certain divine mysteries; (3) that which they were permitted to convey to specific individuals, like the four caliphs and Abu Hurairah. The passage thus clarifies that prophets may have knowledge they do not publicly disclose, but never when commanded to do so.

Key Terms
كتمان
تبليغ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that prophets could hide certain parts of revelation for strategic or social reasons.
Correction: This passage proves that prophets cannot conceal any part of what they are commanded to convey, as doing so would be cursed by Allah.

Checkpoint
What does Dardeer use to prove that prophets cannot conceal?
A) Logical argument
B) Quranic verse
C) Consensus
D) Prophetic hadith

Key Takeaway
Prophets are incapable of concealing any part of the revelation they are commanded to deliver, as made clear by the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Honestly, do you always share the truth when it is difficult or costly, or do you sometimes remain silent to avoid discomfort? How does the curse on concealment confront that silence?
?
Think of a truth you know you should convey to someone but haven't. What is holding you back, and how does this lesson on prophetic responsibility challenge your hesitation?
?
If you were in a position where your words could clarify a misunderstanding but might bring criticism, would you speak or stay quiet? What would it mean for you to imitate the prophets in their commitment to convey?

The Three Categories of What Prophets Were Not Commanded to Convey
Dardeer classifies what prophets were not commanded to convey into three types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of what prophets were not commanded to convey, and which type may be shared with certain individuals.

Core Idea
Not everything a prophet knows must be revealed; some secrets are for select individuals.

While prophets must deliver all commanded revelation, they also possess knowledge that they were not ordered to proclaim. Imam Dardeer classifies this knowledge into three distinct types, ranging from matters of choice to those that must be kept secret. This lesson breaks down that classification, including the special permission to share certain secrets with chosen companions like the four caliphs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation

2
Identify the three categories

3
Consider the examples
Note the examples: divine secrets for the second category, and the four caliphs and Abu Hurairah for the third.

Impossible and Permissible Human Attributes for Prophets
Dardeer enumerates impossible human traits and permissible accidents for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which human traits are impossible for prophets and which are permissible, along with the conditions governing permissible human accidents.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from degrading traits but share permissible human experiences.

Sanusi established the necessity of prophethood and its general attributes. Now Dardeer specifies the human qualities that prophets cannot possess and those they may experience. This lesson clarifies that while prophets are immune to traits like foolishness, they do experience normal human needs—within divinely defined limits. Understanding this balance prevents both extremes: denying their humanity and attributing flaws to them.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the first part of the source passage (up to 'فكل ذلك جائز في حقهم') carefully. Compare with the translation to grasp the precise meaning.
Notice the three impossible traits are listed concisely.
2
Identify impossible and permissible categories
Find the three impossible traits (البلاهة, الغفلة, البلادة) and the conditions for permissible accidents (not forbidden, not degrading, not fatal/repulsive).
The conditions are given in the clause starting with 'بأن'.
3
Examine the examples
See the examples of permissible accidents: essential (eating, drinking, sleep), non-essential (fruits, marriage), and non-fatal diseases. Describe how each fits the conditions.
4
Reflect on the reasoning
Ask yourself: Why are these specific traits impossible? Why are human accidents permissible as long as they don't diminish rank? This connects to the doctrine of prophetic protection.
Impossible traits would negate the purpose of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا يستحيل عليهم البلاهة والغفلة والبلادة. وجائز عليهم كل عرض بشري لا يؤدي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العلية، بأن الجائز لا يكون منهيا عنه، ولا مباحا مزريا، ولا مرضا مؤمنا أو تنافره النفس، كالجذام والبرص، سواء كان مما لا يستغنى عنه عادة كالأكل والشرب والنوم، أم كان مما يستغنى عنه كأكل الفواكه والنكاح، أو كان من الأمراض غير المؤمنة وغير المنفرة، فكل ذلك جائز في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام. ولا تخلو هذه الأعراض النازلة بهم من فوائد: - كتعظيم أجورهم، وعلو مراتبهم عند الله تعالى، والله تعالى وإن كان قادرا على أن يفعل بهم ذلك من غير ابتلاء ومشقة تحصل لهم، إلا أن حكمته تعالى اقتضت ترتب ذلك على الابتلاء، لا يسأل عما يفعل. - وكالتشريع، كما عرفنا أحكام السهو في الصلاة من سهوه، وكيف تؤدى الصلاة في حال المرض والخوف من فعله عليه الصلاة والسلام حال ما ذكر، ودلالة الفعل أقوى من دلالة القول. - وكالتسلية بأحوالهم إذا نزل بنا ما نزل بهم. - وكالتنبيه على حقارة الدنيا وخسة قدرها عند الله تعالى.
Likewise, foolishness, heedlessness, and dullness are impossible for them. And permissible for them is every human accident that does not lead to a deficiency in their lofty ranks, provided that what is permissible is not prohibited, nor a degrading permissible act, nor a deadly disease or one that the soul detests, such as leprosy and vitiligo, whether it is something usually indispensable, like eating, drinking, and sleep, or something dispensable, like eating fruits and marriage, or it is from among non-fatal and non-repulsive diseases. So all of that is permissible in their regard, may blessings and peace be upon them. And these accidents that befall them are not devoid of benefits: such as magnifying their rewards and raising their ranks with Allah, the Exalted—and Allah, the Exalted, although He is able to do that for them without trial and hardship happening to them, yet His wisdom necessitated that it be contingent upon trial; He is not asked about what He does—and such as legislation, as we have learned the rulings of forgetfulness in prayer from his forgetfulness, and how prayer is performed in a state of illness and fear from his action, peace be upon him, in those situations, and the indication of action is stronger than the indication of speech. And such as consolation with their states when what befell them befalls us. And such as drawing attention to the insignificance of this world and the lowliness of its worth with Allah, the Exalted.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive treatment of the human attributes of prophets. It begins by stating three traits that are impossible for them: foolishness (balaha), heedlessness (ghafla), and dullness (balada). Then it explains what is permissible: every human accident (arad bashari) that does not diminish their exalted rank, provided it is not prohibited, not a degrading permissible act, and not a fatal or repulsive disease like leprosy or vitiligo. Permissible acts include necessary ones like eating, drinking, and sleep, and non-necessary ones like eating fruits and marriage. It also includes non-fatal, non-repulsive diseases. Then the author lists four benefits of these accidents: (1) to increase their reward and rank through trials, (2) to legislate rulings (e.g., forgetfulness in prayer, prayer in illness/fear), (3) to console the community by seeing that prophets too faced hardships, and (4) to remind of the insignificance of this world. The passage emphasizes that these are all subject to Allah's wisdom.

Key Terms
البلاهة
الغفلة
البلادة
الأعراض البشرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe prophets should have no human needs or weaknesses whatsoever, to maintain their exalted status.
Correction: The passage shows that prophets do experience human needs and permissible accidents, as long as these do not degrade them or contradict their mission. This balances their humanity and their lofty rank.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for a human accident to be permissible for a prophet?
A) It must not be a prohibited act.
B) It must not be a degrading permissible act.
C) It must be indispensable for daily life.
D) It must not be a fatal or repulsive disease.

Key Takeaway
Prophets are immune from traits that would impair their mission, but they experience permissible human accidents that do not reduce their rank.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a headache or fatigue, do you ever feel it is beneath your spiritual station? How does knowing that prophets, the highest of creation, also endured non-fatal illnesses reshape your patience during such trials? Will you now face your next minor ailment with greater gratitude and acceptance?
?
The passage teaches that even permissible acts can be degrading if they lower one's rank. Think of a habit you consider 'just a small sin' or 'harmless fun' that subtly erodes your spiritual dignity. Are you willing to abandon it today to protect your rank, knowing that prophets avoided even permissible acts that were degrading?
?
Your mission in life, as a follower of the prophets, is to convey truth and embody noble character. Yet you indulge in heedlessness and dullness of heart regularly. What is one practical step you will take this week to sharpen your spiritual awareness, so you do not resemble the very traits impossible for prophets?

The Wisdom Behind Prophets' Human Accidents
Dardeer lists four benefits of prophets experiencing human accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four benefits of prophets experiencing human accidents, as explained by Imam Dardeer.

Core Idea
Prophetic human accidents serve wisdom: reward, legislation, consolation, and perspective.

Having established that prophets experience permissible human accidents, Dardeer now explains why these are not in vain. Each accident carries divine wisdom. This lesson explores the four benefits he lists: increasing reward, providing legal rulings, comforting the community, and reminding of the world's insignificance. These benefits show that even the trials of prophets are part of Allah's wise plan.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read from 'ولا تخلو هذه الأعراض' to the end. Identify the four benefits explicitly mentioned.
Each benefit is introduced by the letter 'كاف' (like 'ك', 'و', 'و').
2
Understand each benefit
For each benefit, consider: (1) How does it relate to the prophet himself? (2) How does it benefit the community? (3) What wisdom does it reveal about Allah?
The first benefit is about reward, second about legislation, third about consolation, fourth about worldly insignificance.
3
Reflect on the legislation benefit
Notice that the author gives specific examples: rulings of forgetfulness in prayer from the Prophet's own forgetfulness, and prayer during illness and fear from his actions. He emphasizes that action is stronger than speech in evidence.
This shows that prophets' actions are a source of legal rulings.
4
Connect to the broader Islamic worldview
Ask yourself: How does this teaching affect my understanding of prophets? Allah's wisdom is not arbitrary—these benefits show purpose behind trials.

Source Text

It begins by stating three traits that are impossible for them: foolishness (balaha), heedlessness (ghafla), and dullness (balada). Then it explains what is permissible: every human accident (arad bashari) that does not diminish their exalted rank, provided it is not prohibited, not a degrading permissible act, and not a fatal or repulsive disease like leprosy or vitiligo. Permissible acts include necessary ones like eating, drinking, and sleep, and non-necessary ones like eating fruits and marriage. It also includes non-fatal, non-repulsive diseases. Then the author lists four benefits of these accidents: (1) to increase their reward and rank through trials, (2) to legislate rulings (e.g., forgetfulness in prayer, prayer in illness/fear), (3) to console the community by seeing that prophets too faced hardships, and (4) to remind of the insignificance of this world. The passage emphasizes that these are all subject to Allah's wisdom.

Key Terms
الابتلاء
التشريع
التسلية
حقارة الدنيا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that prophets' trials are meaningless or unjust, or that they indicate Allah's displeasure.
Correction: The passage shows that these trials are filled with wisdom: they increase reward, provide legal guidance, console believers, and remind of the world's true value. They are part of Allah's perfect plan.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the benefits mentioned for prophets' human accidents?
A) Magnifying their rewards and ranks
B) Providing legislation through their actions
C) Demonstrating that prophets are not subject to human emotions
D) Drawing attention to the insignificance of this world

Key Takeaway
Prophetic trials are not in vain; they serve profound wisdom: increasing reward, legislating rulings, comforting believers, and teaching the true value of this world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial, do you immediately feel that Allah is punishing you? This lesson teaches that even the prophets were tested for greater rewards. Will you now try to shift your first thought from 'Why me?' to 'What wisdom is behind this?'
?
The Prophet’s actions in illness and fear became law for the community. Have you considered that your own conduct in hardship might influence others? Are you living in a way that would console or guide someone who looks up to you?
?
The fourth wisdom is to recognize the low worth of this world. Look at your life: where does your attachment to worldly comfort surpass your desire for the hereafter? Name one specific attachment you will intentionally let go of starting today.

The Possible Human Attributes of Prophets
Dardeer defines permissible human accidents for prophets and their conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what human accidents are possible for prophets and the conditions that make an accident permissible or impermissible.

Core Idea
Prophets experience human needs, but never degrading or fatal flaws.

Dardeer now clarifies the possible human attributes of prophets. Since prophets are human, they share many physical and psychological experiences with us. However, not every human accident is permissible for them. This passage sets the boundaries, ensuring nothing diminishes their exalted rank. Let's examine the conditions and examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall meaning.
2
Identify the central condition
Notice the condition for a human accident to be possible: it must not lead to deficiency in the prophets' high rank. This is the key principle.
The Arabic phrase is 'لا يؤدي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العليّة'.
3
Understand the three excluded categories
Find the three types of accidents that are excluded: prohibited acts, degrading permissible acts, and fatal or repulsive diseases. These would cause deficiency.
4
Explore the permissible categories with examples
The passage lists three permissible categories: unavoidable needs (eating, drinking, sleep), avoidable but non-degrading acts (fruits, marriage), and non-fatal, non-repulsive diseases. Each is possible for prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في حق الرسل: وجائز عليهم كل عرض بشري لا يؤدي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العليّة، بأن الجائز لا يكون منهيا عنه، ولا مباحاً مزرياً، ولا مرضاً مؤمناً أو تعافه النفس، كالجذام والبرص، سواء كان مما لا يستغنى عنه عادةً كالأكل والشرب والنوم، أم كان مما يستغنى عنه كأكل الفواكه والنكاح، أو كان من الأمراض غير المؤمنة وغير المنفرة، فكل ذلك جائز في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام.
Regarding the messengers: and it is possible for them every human accident that does not lead to deficiency in their high ranks, such that the possible is not prohibited, nor a degrading permissible act, nor a fatal disease or one that the soul abhors, like leprosy and vitiligo, whether it is something not usually dispensed with like eating, drinking, and sleeping, or something dispensed with like eating fruits and marriage, or it is from diseases that are not fatal and not repulsive; all of that is possible for them, peace be upon them.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage classifies the type of human experiences that are possible (jāʾiz) for prophets. After stating that it is possible for them to have any human accident (ʿaraḍ basharī) that does not diminish their high station, the author lists three conditions that make an accident unacceptable: (1) being prohibited (manhiyy ʿanh), (2) being a degrading permissible act (mubāḥ muzrī), or (3) being a fatal disease (maraḍ muʾmin) or one that people naturally find repulsive. He then gives examples of permissible accidents: those habitually unavoidable (eating, drinking, sleep), those avoidable but not degrading (fruits, marriage), and non-fatal, non-repulsive diseases. The conclusion is that all such accidents are possible for prophets.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets cannot experience any human limitations or needs.
Correction: Prophets can experience non-degrading human accidents like eating, sleeping, and non-fatal illnesses, as long as they do not lower their rank.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Prophets experience natural human needs but never any defect that lowers their status.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Four Benefits of Prophets' Human Trials
Dardeer enumerates four wisdom benefits underlying prophets' human experiences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four wisdom benefits that Allah attaches to the human experiences of prophets, including increased reward, legislative guidance, comfort for believers, and detachment from worldly attachment.

Core Idea
Prophets' trials serve multiple divine wisdoms: reward, law, comfort, and detachment.

Dardeer explains that the hardships prophets face are not random but carry profound benefits. He enumerates four distinct wisdoms: they elevate the prophets' ranks, provide rulings for the community, offer comfort to believers in their own trials, and teach the insignificance of the world. This passage invites us to see divine wisdom even in affliction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Dardeer uses a numbered list format with '--' to introduce each benefit.
2
Identify the four benefits
The passage lists four benefits. Find each one and notice how Dardeer defines it: magnification of rewards and ranks, legislation, consolation, and attention to the world's contemptibility.
Each benefit begins with a kaaf (like) and is followed by a specific explanation.
3
Examine the supporting hadith
The fourth benefit is illustrated by a hadith: 'If the world were worth a mosquito's wing to Allah...' Reflect on how this hadith reinforces the lesson of detachment.
The hadith shows the extreme low value of the world in Allah's sight.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends by describing the response of the intelligent person: turning away from the world and attaching his heart to Allah, expecting a praiseworthy outcome after death.
This practical application ties the benefits to personal spirituality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تخلو هذه الأعراض النازلة بهم من فوائد: - كتعظيم أجورهم، وعلو مراتبهم عند الله تعالى، والله تعالى وإن كان قادراً على أن يفعل بهم ذلك من غير ابتلاء ومشقة تحصل لهم، إلا أن حكمته تعالى اقتضت ترتب ذلك على الابتلاء، لا يسأل عما يفعل. - وكالتشريع، كما عرفنا أحكام السهو في الصلاة من سهوه، وكيف تؤدى الصلاة في حال المرض والخوف من فعله عليه الصلاة والسلام حال ما ذكر، ودلالة الفعل أقوى من دلالة القول. - وكالتسلي بأحوالهم إذا نزل بنا ما نزل بهم. - وكالتنبيه على حقارة الدنيا وخسة قدرها عند الله تعالى. ولذا قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: (لو كانت الدنيا تزن عند الله جناح بعوضة ما سقى الكافر منها جرعة ماء). فإذا نظر العاقل في أحوالهم - عليهم الصلاة والسلام - من أمراض وأسقام وقلة مال وأذية الخلق لهم علم أنها لا قدر لها عند الله تعالى فأعرض عنها بقلبه بالكلية، وعلق قلبه بربه في البكرة والعشية إن كان ذا همة عليّة، حتى يرى إثر موته عاقبة هذه العيشة المرضية.
And these accidents that befall them are not devoid of benefits: - Like magnifying their rewards and raising their ranks with Allah Almighty, and although Allah Almighty is able to do that to them without trial and hardship occurring to them, His wisdom necessitated that it be attached to trial; He is not asked about what He does. - And like legislation, as we learned the rulings of forgetfulness in prayer from his forgetfulness, and how prayer is performed in a state of illness and fear from his action, peace be upon him, at the time mentioned, and the indication of action is stronger than the indication of speech. - And like consolation through their conditions when what befell them befalls us. - And like drawing attention to the contemptibility of the world and the lowness of its value with Allah Almighty. Hence he, peace be upon him, said: 'If the world were worth a mosquito's wing to Allah, He would not give a disbeliever a sip of water from it.' So when the intelligent person looks at their conditions - peace be upon them - of illnesses, ailments, lack of wealth, and the harm of people to them, he knows that it has no value with Allah Almighty, so he turns away from it completely with his heart, and attaches his heart to his Lord morning and evening, if he has high ambition, until he sees after his death the outcome of this praiseworthy life.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage lists four benefits (fawāʾid) that result from prophets experiencing human accidents. First, these trials increase their reward and rank; although Allah could grant this without trial, His wisdom attached it to trial. Second, it provides legislation (tashrīʿ) for believers, as in the rulings on forgetfulness in prayer learned from the Prophet's own forgetfulness, and how to pray in illness or fear from his actual practice, because action has stronger evidence than speech. Third, it offers consolation (tasallī) for believers when they face similar trials. Fourth, it alerts believers to the world's insignificance before Allah, supported by the hadith that the world is worth less than a mosquito's wing. The passage concludes that a wise person, seeing the prophets' hardships, will detach from this world and focus on the Hereafter.

ابتلاء

حقارة الدنيا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think trials are arbitrary or pointless.
Correction: The author shows that trials have clear divine wisdom: they increase reward, provide legislation, offer consolation, and teach detachment from the world.

Checkpoint

A) It proves their humanity

Permissible and Impermissible Accidents for Prophets
Dardeer clarifies examples of permissible and impermissible accidents for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which human accidents are permissible or impermissible for prophets, focusing on degrading permissible acts and fatal diseases.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from degrading acts and fatal diseases, but forgetfulness in actions is allowed.

Imam Dardeer continues his explanation of what is permissible for prophets. In this passage, he gives concrete examples of actions and conditions that are impossible for them, such as begging, blindness, and madness. He also clarifies that forgetfulness in actions is permissible but not in statements. Read on to see the specific rulings.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Note that the passage cuts off at the end; we cover what is available.
2
Identify the two categories being clarified
The passage explains two categories: 'al-mubāḥ al-muzrī' (degrading permissible act) and 'al-maraḍ al-muʾmin' (fatal disease). Find their definitions and examples.
3
Understand the examples of degrading acts
Note that asking for charity, even accepting it, is not allowed for prophets, and eating in the market is considered degrading.
This shows prophets are protected from actions that lower their dignity.
4
Understand the examples of fatal diseases
Blindness and madness, even minor, are impossible for prophets because they are fatal and cause deficiency. The author refutes claims that Shu'ayb or Ya'qub were blind.
Temporary conditions like Ya'qub's loss of sight are not considered permanent blindness.
5
Examine the exception for forgetfulness
Forgetfulness (sahw) is permissible in actions, like the Prophet's salam from two rak'ahs, but not in statements (revelation). Reflect on why this distinction matters.
The text begins discussing forgetfulness (nisyān) but cuts off; we base our understanding on the available part.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودخل في قولنا «المباح المزري» سؤال الصدقة، بل قبولها، فلا يجوز عليهم، والأكل في السوق. ودخل في «المرض المؤمن» العمى والجنون ولو قل، لأن شأنه أن يؤمن، ولأنه نقص، ولم يعم نبي قط، وما قيل: إن شعيباً العلم كان ضريرا.. لا أصل له، ويعقوب إنما حصلت له غشاوة وزالت. وأما السهو فيجوز في الأفعال كالسلام من ركعتين، دون الأقوال، وأما نسيان...
And there enters into our statement 'the degrading permissible act': asking for charity, rather accepting it, so it is not allowed for them, and eating in the market. And there enters into 'the fatal disease': blindness and madness, even if slight, because their nature is to be fatal, and because it is deficiency, and no prophet has ever been blind, and what is said: that Shu'ayb the knowledgeable was blind... has no basis, and Ya'qub only had a covering and it was removed. As for forgetfulness, it is permissible in actions, like the greeting from two rak'ahs, but not in statements; and as for forgetting...
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage clarifies two categories mentioned earlier: the degrading permissible act (al-mubāḥ al-muzrī) and the fatal disease (al-maraḍ al-muʾmin). First, examples of degrading permissible acts: begging (asking for charity) is not allowed for prophets; even accepting charity is not allowed, and eating in the market is also degrading. Second, examples of fatal diseases: blindness and madness, even if slight, are impossible because they are fatal and cause deficiency. The author refutes claims that any prophet was blind: the story of Shu'ayb being blind has no basis, and Ya'qub's loss of sight was temporary. The passage then discusses forgetfulness (sahw): it is permissible for prophets in actions (e.g., the Prophet's salam after two rak'ahs due to forgetfulness) but not in statements (i.e., in conveying revelation). The text cuts off while beginning a discussion on forgetfulness (nisyān).

Correction: Prophets are protected from actions that degrade their status and from fatal diseases that cause permanent deficiency, though temporary conditions like Ya'qub's loss of sight are possible.

The Worthlessness of the World and the Prophets' Example
Dardeer explains the hadith about the world's insignificance and its implication for the prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the profound insignificance of the world in Allah's sight and how the prophets' lives exemplify this truth.

Core Idea
The world is worth less than a mosquito's wing to Allah.

This lesson explores a powerful hadith that reveals the true value of the world. By reflecting on the lives of the prophets—who endured hardship and poverty—we learn to detach from worldly pursuits and attach ourselves to Allah. The passage calls us to a higher aspiration.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Start by reading the hadith: 'If the world weighed with Allah the wing of a mosquito, He would not give a disbeliever a sip of water from it.' Notice the extreme contrast: the entire world is less than a mosquito's wing.
The hadith is narrated in several collections; its authenticity is well-established.
2
Consider the prophets' conditions
The author then invites you to look at the prophets' lives: illnesses, poverty, and harm from people. Ask yourself why they suffered despite being the best of creation.
This reflection leads to the conclusion that the world has no value with Allah.
3
Apply the lesson to yourself
The intelligent person turns away from the world and attaches his heart to Allah. If you have high aspiration, you will focus on the afterlife and await its reward.
The passage ends with a hopeful note: the pleasing outcome after death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولذا قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: (لو كانتِ الدُّنيا تزِنُ عِندَ اللهِ جَناحَ بعوضة ما سقى الكافر منها جرعة ماء) (۱). فإذا نظر العاقل في أحوالهم - عليهم الصلاة والسلام - مِنْ أمراض وأسقام وقِلَّةِ مال وأذيَّةِ الخَلْقِ لهم علِمَ أنها لا قدر لها عند الله تعالى فأعرض عنها بقلبه بالكلية، وعلَّقَ قلبه برَبِّه في البُكْرةِ والعَشيّة إنْ كانَ ذا همة عليّةٍ، حتى يرى إثْرَ مَوتِه عاقبة هذه العيشةِ المَرْضِيّةِ
And therefore he (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'If the world weighed with Allah the wing of a mosquito, He would not give a disbeliever a sip of water from it' (1). So when the intelligent person looks at their conditions—peace and blessings be upon them—of illnesses, ailments, scarcity of wealth, and harm from creation, he knows that it has no value with Allah Almighty, so he turns away from it completely with his heart, and attaches his heart to his Lord morning and evening, if he is of high aspiration, until he sees after his death the outcome of this pleasing life.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an explanation and moral lesson derived from a hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ). The hadith states that if the entire world were worth the wing of a mosquito in Allah's sight, He would not give a disbeliever even a sip of water. This shows the extreme insignificance of the world. The author then draws a conclusion: when an intelligent person considers the conditions of the prophets—their illnesses, poverty, and harm from people—he realizes that the world has no value with Allah. Consequently, he should turn away from it entirely and instead attach his heart to Allah at all times, if he has high aspiration. The ultimate reward is seen after death.

جناح بعوضة
العاقل
الهمة العليّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the prophets' sufferings indicate Allah's displeasure or punishment.
Correction: The hadith shows that the world is worthless; thus prophets' lack of worldly comfort is a sign of honor and detachment, not displeasure.

Checkpoint

B) The world is worthless, so their lack of comfort is a sign of honor.
C) The prophets were ungrateful.
D) The world is valuable but the prophets rejected it.

Key Takeaway
The hadith demonstrates the world's worthlessness, and the prophets' hardships confirm that true value lies in the Hereafter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

When you face hardship or lack, do you complain or turn to Allah? How would your reaction change if you deeply internalized that the prophets—the best of creation—suffered worse, not because Allah is angry, but because this world is worthless?
?
Examine your morning and evening routine: what is your heart attached to? If you claim to be of high aspiration, where is your energy directed—toward the world or toward your Lord? Will you commit to turning your heart away from one worldly attachment today?

Permissible Human Experiences for Prophets
Dardeer lists impermissible lowly actions and grievous ailments for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which lowly actions and grievous ailments are impermissible for prophets according to Sunni theology.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from deficiencies that cause grief or disgrace.

Imam Dardeer's commentary on al-Kharidah clarifies the boundaries of what prophets may experience as humans. It distinguishes between permissible acts that are neutral and those considered lowly or grievous, emphasizing that prophets are shielded from such deficiencies. The passage specifically addresses asking for charity, accepting it, eating in the market, blindness, and madness, and refutes claims that any prophet ever became blind.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the full Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Notice the precise terms used.
2
Identify the two categories
Find the two categories: 'المباح المزري' (disgraceful permissible) and 'المرض المؤمن' (calamity causing grief). Understand what each includes.
3
Understand the examples
For the first category: asking for charity, accepting charity, eating in the market. For the second: blindness and madness. Note why each is problematic.
4
Examine the refutation
The author refutes the claim that any prophet became blind, specifically addressing Shu'ayb and Ya'qub.
5
Reflect on the theological principle
Consider the underlying principle: prophets are protected from deficiencies that cause grief or disgrace, preserving their dignity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودخل في قولنا «المباحُ المزري» سؤالُ الصَّدَقَةِ، بَلْ قبولها، فلا يجوز عليهم، والأكل في السوق. ودخل في «المَرَضِ المُؤْمِنِ» العمى والجُنونُ ولَو قل، لأنَّ شأنه أنْ يُؤْمِنَ، ولأنه نقص، ولم يعْمَ نبي قط، وما قيل: إِنَّ شُعَيبا العلم كان ضريرا.. لا أصل له، ويعقوب إنما حصلت له غشاوة وزالت (۳).
And included in our statement 'the disgraceful permissible' is asking for charity, rather accepting it, so it is not permissible for them, and eating in the market. And included in 'the calamity that causes grief' is blindness and madness, even if little, because its nature is to cause grief, and because it is a deficiency, and no prophet ever became blind, and what was said that Shu'ayb (peace be upon him) was blind... has no basis, and Ya'qub only had a covering that later lifted (3).
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage classifies what is permissible for prophets among human experiences. It first addresses the 'disgraceful permissible' (المباح المزري): actions that are permissible for ordinary people but considered lowly. The author states that asking for charity, and even accepting it, is not permissible for prophets. Similarly, eating in the market is not permissible. Then it discusses the 'calamity that causes grief' (المرض المؤمن) such as blindness and madness. These are not permissible because they cause grief and are deficiencies. The author asserts that no prophet ever became blind, refuting the claim that Prophet Shu'ayb was blind. As for Prophet Ya'qub, his loss of sight was only a covering that later lifted, not true blindness.

Key Terms
المباح المزري
المرض المؤمن
العمى
الجُنون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets can experience any human ailment, including blindness.
Correction: Blindness is a deficiency that prophets are protected from, as it causes grief and diminishes dignity. No prophet ever became blind.

Checkpoint
Which condition does the author state never occurred to any prophet?
A) Poverty
B) Blindness
C) Sickness
D) Persecution

Key Takeaway
Prophets are immune from disgraceful actions and grievous deficiencies like blindness, preserving their dignity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a temptation to do something permissible but lowly (like consuming content that wastes time or engaging in gossip), how does knowing that prophets avoided even the 'disgraceful permissible' challenge you to raise your own standards? What is one lowly habit you will actively replace this week with something that honors your dignity as a believer?
?
The prophets were protected from even minor bodily deficiencies that cause grief, like temporary blindness. How does this complete perfection of their physical state affect the way you regard them and the guidance they brought? Are you ever casual in your reverence for the prophets? What concrete change can you make in your daily life to demonstrate deeper love and respect for them?
?
If a prophet like Ya'qub could experience temporary grief but not permanent deficiency, how does that reshape your understanding of trials in your own life? Are you willing to accept that your own struggles, though painful, are not a sign of divine displeasure but rather a test for growth? What step will you take this week to turn a current trial into an act of worship?

Forgetfulness in Prophets: Actions vs. Words
Dardeer rules on forgetfulness in prophets, distinguishing actions, words, and rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nuanced ruling on forgetfulness for prophets, distinguishing between actions, words, and rulings at different times.

Core Idea
Prophets can forget in actions but not words; rulings are safeguarded after delivery.

Imam Dardeer clarifies a subtle aspect of prophetic infallibility: forgetfulness is not entirely prohibited. While prophets never err in conveying revelation, they may experience forgetfulness in certain actions and in rulings after they have been delivered. This passage delineates these boundaries.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp Dardeer's categorizations.
2
Distinguish actions from words
Notice that forgetfulness in actions (like the salam mistake) is permissible, but forgetfulness in words is not. Reflect on why this distinction exists.
The action example comes from a hadith.
3
Understand the timing for rulings
Identify the two time periods: before delivery (forgetfulness not allowed) vs after delivery (allowed). Also note the special case of abrogated rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما السَّهْرُ فيجوزُ في الأفعالِ كالسلامِ مِنْ رَكْعَتَينِ (٤)، دونَ الأقوال، وأما نسيان الأحكام فلا يجوز عليهم قبل التبليغ، ويجوزُ بَعْدَه لِحِفْظِهِ بَعدَه، ولوجوب ضَبطه على وليُبَلِّغَه، ويجوز نسيان المنسوخ ما قبل التبليغ وبعده.
And as for forgetfulness, it is permissible in actions, like the greeting after two rak'ahs (4), but not in words. And as for forgetting rulings, it is not permissible for them before delivery, and it is permissible after it, for the preservation of it after it, and because it is necessary to preserve it so that he can deliver it, and forgetting the abrogated is permissible before and after delivery.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage defines the scope of forgetfulness (السهو) permissible for prophets. Forgetfulness in actions, such as the Prophet once greeting after two rak'ahs (as in the hadith of Dhul-Yadain), is permissible. However, forgetfulness in words (statements) is not permissible. Regarding rulings (الأحكام), the author distinguishes: before delivering the revelation, forgetfulness is not permissible because they must convey it accurately. After delivery, it becomes permissible because the ruling has been preserved through the ummah. Forgetting abrogated rulings (المنسوخ) is permissible both before and after delivery, as it no longer matters.

Key Terms
السهو
الأفعال
الأقوال
الأحكام
المنسوخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets cannot forget anything whatsoever.
Correction: They can forget in actions and in rulings after delivery, but not in words or in rulings before delivery.

Checkpoint
When is forgetfulness in rulings permissible for prophets?
A) Before delivery
B) After delivery
C) Both
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Prophets are protected from forgetfulness in speech and before delivering rulings, but may forget in actions and after rulings are preserved.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet ﷺ forgot in prayer, yet he was the most beloved to Allah. When you forget in your worship, do you turn away in frustration or do you humbly return to your Lord, knowing that He accepts your imperfection? What will you do the next time you make a mistake in salah?
?
If the Prophet ﷺ was so careful not to forget his words, how much more careful should you be when you speak about Allah's religion? Is there a word you've spoken carelessly about faith that you need to repent for today?
?
The rulings were preserved after delivery, and you have the Qur'an and sunnah at your fingertips. Are you actively preserving them in your heart and life? What one verse or hadith will you commit to memory and practice starting today?

Prophets' Inward State Unaffected by Outward Trials
Dardeer explains that prophets' outward experiences do not affect their inner devotion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets' outward human experiences do not affect their profound inner connection with Allah, but rather increase their closeness and love.

Core Idea
Prophets' trials only deepen their love and closeness to Allah.

This lesson explores a key distinction in Islamic theology: the prophets' outward humanity does not compromise their inward perfection. We will see how Saint Dardeer explains that their hearts remain filled with divine love despite any trials.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through.
Notice the contrast between outward appearances and inward states.
2
Identify the outward/inward distinction
The passage clearly separates what happens to prophets' outward selves from their inward selves. Mark these two parts.
3
Understand the effect of trials
Notice that the prophets do not feel distress, complaint, or aversion. Instead, the trials increase their closeness and love for Allah.
This is a key point: trials are transformative, not detrimental.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider that even many of their followers achieve this state, so the prophets are the highest example. This confirms their unique station.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن ما جاز عليهم مِنَ الأعراض البشريّةِ التي لا تؤدّي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العليّة، فإنما هو بحسَب ظواهرهم فقط، وأما بواطنهم فهي معمورة بالأسرار الإلهية، متعلقةٌ بِحُبِّ خالقِ البَريَّة، فلا يُحْصُلُ مِنهم ضَجَرٌ ولا شكوى ولا ناؤُه منها، بل لا يزيدُهم منه إلا قُربا وحُبَّا، بل هذه الحالةُ تكونُ في كثير مِنْ أُمَّتِهم، فكيف بهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام !

Instead, these conditions increase their closeness and love for Allah. The author emphasizes that even many of their followers achieve such a state, so the prophets themselves are even more elevated.

Objections to Prophethood and Their Refutation (Introduction)
Dardeer presents Mu'tazila, Samaniyya, and Barahima views on prophethood necessity and hints at refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila argument for the necessity of sending prophets, the objection by the Samaniyya and Barahima, and why this issue requires a response from Sunni theology.

Core Idea
Prophethood is not futile; reason alone is insufficient.

Dardeer begins by presenting the views of three groups on whether Allah must send prophets. The Mu'tazila argue it is obligatory based on divine goodness, while the Samaniyya and Barahima reject it as unnecessary. This sets up the need for a Sunni refutation, which Dardeer will provide next.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the flow of argument.
Notice that the passage ends abruptly with 'He pointed to the refutation...'
2
Identify the groups mentioned
The passage mentions three groups: Mu'tazila, Samaniyya, and Barahima. Understand their positions.
Mu'tazila are a rationalist sect; Samaniyya and Barahima are non-Muslim groups denying prophethood.
3
Analyze the Mu'tazila position
The Mu'tazila argue that sending prophets is obligatory (wajib) upon Allah because it is the most beneficial (aslah) for His servants. This is based on their principle that Allah must do what is best.
Sunni theology rejects imposing obligations on Allah.
4
Understand the objection
The Samaniyya and Barahima reject this, calling it futile (abath) because human intellect is sufficient for guidance.
This objection denies the necessity of prophethood altogether.
5
Reflect on the refutation signal
Dardeer indicates he will refute these views. Think about why a refutation is needed: the intellect alone cannot guide to all truths, especially matters of the unseen.
The actual refutation is not in this passage but will follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما أوجبتِ المُعتَزِلةُ إرسالَ الرُّسُلِ بِناءً على قاعدتهم، مِنْ وُجوبِ الصلاحِ عليه تعالى، والأصلحُ في حَقٌّ عبيده أنْ يُرسِلَ إليهم الرُّسُلَ ليُنبهوهم على ما يُنَجِّيهم مِنَ المهالِكِ وما يُوبقُهم فيها ، وأحاله السَّمْنِيَّةُ (۳) والبراهمة؛ نظرًا إلى أنه عبث؛ لكون العقل كافيًا عنه .. أشار إلى الرَّدِّ عليهم بقوله:
And when the Mu'tazila obligated the sending of messengers based on their principle of the obligation of what is beneficial (al-salah) upon Him, Most High, and the most beneficial for His servants is to send them messengers to warn them of what saves them from perils and what causes them to perish, the Samaniyya (3) and the Barahima deemed it impossible; considering it to be futile, because the intellect is sufficient for it. He pointed to the refutation of them by his saying:
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents the positions of different groups regarding the necessity of sending prophets. The Mu'tazila argue that it is obligatory (واجب) upon Allah to send messengers because it is beneficial (صلاح) and the most beneficial (أصلح) for humanity. This is based on their rationalist principle that Allah must do what is best for His creation. In contrast, the Samaniyya and Barahima (Hindu groups) reject the necessity, arguing that sending prophets is futile (عبث) because human reason (العقل) is sufficient to guide people. The author then indicates that he will refute these views, but the actual refutation text is not fully given in this window.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
وجوب الصلاح
الأصلح
السَّمْنِيَّة
البراهمة
العبث
العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human reason is completely sufficient for guidance, making prophets unnecessary.
Correction: While reason is important, it cannot fully guide humanity; prophets bring revelation that reason cannot access.

Checkpoint
Why do the Samaniyya and Barahima consider the sending of prophets futile?
A) Because prophets often cause conflict
B) Because human intellect is sufficient for guidance
C) Because Allah does not need to send them
D) Because they are not needed for salvation

Key Takeaway
This passage introduces the debate on prophethood necessity, highlighting the Mu'tazila's rational obligation and the intellectualist objection that prophets are unnecessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely on your own intellect to decide matters of faith, or do you recognize the limits of reason? In what area of your life have you trusted your reasoning over divine guidance, and what was the result?
?
The Mu'tazila thought they were honoring Allah by making His actions subject to their concept of 'most beneficial'. Are there ways in which you, perhaps unknowingly, impose your own standards on Allah? Examine your expectations of how Allah should treat you.
?
The Samaniyya and Barahima rejected prophets because they thought reason was sufficient. Have you ever minimized the need for prophetic guidance by thinking that your own understanding is enough? Where do you need to submit to revelation rather than your own opinion?

The Prophets' Outer Human Experiences and Inner Divine Connection
Explains the permissible human experiences of prophets and their inner state.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how prophets can experience human accidents outwardly while maintaining an inner state of divine attachment and perfection.

Core Idea
Prophets' inner selves remain pure and attached to God even during human experiences.

This passage from Imam Dardir's commentary clarifies a key aspect of prophetic infallibility: while prophets may experience ordinary human states such as hunger or fatigue in their outer lives, their inner selves are entirely devoted to God. Understanding this distinction helps prevent misconceptions about the prophets' spiritual perfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the contrast between 'ظواهرهم' (their outer appearances) and 'بواطنهم' (their inner selves).
The author uses the word 'واعلم' (and know) to emphasize the importance of this principle.
2
Identify the key distinction
The passage states that human accidents are permissible for prophets only in their outer appearances. Their inner selves are filled with divine secrets and love for God. Identify the phrases that describe each.
3
Reflect on the consequence and generalization
Notice that the inner state prevents distress, complaint, and aversion. Then observe how the author extends this state to many in the community, making an argument from the greater to the lesser.
This strengthens the affirmation of prophetic perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن ما جازَ عليهم مِنَ الأعراض البشريّةِ التي لا تؤدّي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العلية، فإنما هو بحسَب ظواهرهم فقط، وأما بواطنهم فهي معمورة بالأسرار الإلهية، متعلقةٌ بِحُبِّ خالقِ البَريَّة، فلا يُحْصُلُ مِنهم ضَجَرٌ ولا شكوى ولا ناؤُه منها، بل لا يزيدُهم منه إلا قُربا وحُبَّا، بل هذه الحالةُ تكونُ في كثير مِنْ أُمَّتِهم، فكيف بهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام !
And know that what is permissible for them of human accidents that do not lead to deficiency in their high ranks, it is only according to their outer appearances, but as for their inner selves, they are filled with divine secrets, attached to the love of the Creator of creation, so no distress, complaint, or aversion comes from them; rather, it only increases them in closeness and love. Indeed, this state occurs in many of their community, so how about them, blessings and peace be upon them!
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the nature of prophets' human experiences. The author begins by stating a principle: any human accidents (الأعراض البشرية) that do not lead to a deficiency in their high ranks are permissible for prophets, but only in their outward appearances (ظواهرهم). He then contrasts this with their inner selves (بواطنهم), which are filled with divine secrets and attached solely to love of God. The consequence of this inner state is that no distress, complaint, or aversion emanates from them. On the contrary, such experiences only increase them in closeness and love to God. The author then generalizes that this elevated state is found even among many of their followers, so it is certainly so for the prophets themselves. The passage thus affirms the prophets' inner infallibility and spiritual perfection despite outward human experiences.

Correction: The passage clarifies that while prophets may outwardly experience human accidents, their inner selves remain free from distress, complaint, and aversion, and are instead filled with divine secrets and love for God.

Sending Messengers: A Favor, Not an Obligation
Refutes views on necessity of sending messengers and states it is a favor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why sending messengers is a favor and mercy from Allah, not an obligation, based on His nature as the free agent and the insufficiency of reason alone.

Core Idea
Sending messengers is a free gift from Allah, not a debt He owes.

In this passage, the author addresses a key theological debate: Is it obligatory for Allah to send prophets? Some groups argued yes, others no. The author clarifies that sending messengers is a favor and mercy, rooted in Allah's absolute freedom and the limits of human reason.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Read the passage and note the views of the Mu'tazila, the Samaniyya, and the Barahima regarding the sending of messengers.
The Mu'tazila say it is obligatory; the Samaniyya and Barahima say it is impossible or frivolous.
2
Understand the author's refutation
Focus on the line: 'Sending them is a favor and mercy…' and how the author uses it to reject both extremes.
The author emphasizes that it is a favor, not obligatory.
3
Grasp the supporting arguments
The author gives two reasons: Allah is the free agent who is not compelled, and the intellect alone cannot grasp the subtleties of divine law.
Reflect on why reason is insufficient for these matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما أوجبتِ المُعتَزِلةُ إرسالَ الرُّسُلِ بِناءً على قاعدتهم، مِنْ وُجوبِ الصلاحِ عليه تعالى، والأصلحُ في حَقٌّ عبيده أنْ يُرسِلَ إليهم الرُّسُلَ ليُنبهوهم على ما يُنَجِّيهم مِنَ المهالِكِ وما يُوبقُهم فيها ، وأحاله السَّمْنِيَّةُ والبراهمة؛ نظرًا إلى أنه عبث؛ لكون العقل كافيًا عنه .. أشار إلى الرَّدِّ عليهم بقوله: إرسالهم تفَضَّل ورحمة * للعالمينَ جَلَّ مُولِي النَّعْمة إرسالهم تفَضُّل وإحسانٌ مِنَ اللهِ تعالى، ورحمةٌ مِنه للعالمين وليس بواجب عليه، لما علمت أنه الفاعلُ المُختارُ الذي لا حرج عليه، ولا يُسأل عما يفعلُ، ولا بمُستحيل؛ لأنَّ العقل إذا خلا ونفسَه قد يعْفُلُ عنْ أكثر الأحوالِ المناسبة له في معاشه، فكيف بدقائقِ الشَّرْع والسَّمْعياتِ التي لا تُتلقى إلا مِنَ الصَّادِقِ. جلَّ مُولي بضَم الميم وكسْرِ اللام، أي: مُعْطي، النِّعْمةِ التي مِنْ أَجَلَّها إرسال الرُّسُل إلينا، فلهُ الحَمْدُ على ذلك، وعلى كل حال.
And when the Mu'tazila deemed it obligatory to send messengers, based on their principle of the obligation of what is good and the most good upon God—that the most good for His servants is to send them messengers to alert them to what saves them from perils and what destroys them—and the Samaniyya and Barahima deemed it impossible, considering it frivolous because the intellect is sufficient, he (the author) indicated the refutation of them by saying: 'Sending them is a favor and mercy for the worlds, exalted is the Bestower of grace.' Sending them is a favor and beneficence from God Almighty and mercy from Him for the worlds, and it is not obligatory upon Him, because you have known that He is the free agent who is under no compulsion, nor is He asked about what He does, nor is it impossible; because the intellect, left to itself, often neglects most of the circumstances suitable for its livelihood, so how about the subtleties of the Law and the revealed matters that are only received from the truthful one. 'Exalted is the Bestower,' with damma on the mim and kasra on the lam, meaning the giver, 'of grace,' the greatest of which is the sending of messengers to us. So to Him is praise for that and for every state.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents a theological argument regarding the necessity of sending messengers. The author first states the position of the Mu'tazila, who—based on their principle that God must do what is good and best (الصلاح والأصلح)—deem it obligatory for God to send messengers to guide humanity. He then contrasts this with the rejection of the Samaniyya and Barahima, who consider sending messengers to be futile (عبث) because they claim human reason is sufficient. The author then refutes both by citing his own poetic line: 'Sending them is a favor and mercy for the worlds.' In his explanation, he emphasizes that sending messengers is a favor (تفضل) and mercy (رحمة) from God, not an obligation, because God is the free agent (الفاعل المختار) who is not constrained, questioned, or subject to impossibility. He further argues that reason alone is insufficient, as it often fails to grasp even worldly affairs, let alone the subtleties of divine law and revelation, which can only be received from a truthful messenger. The passage closes by praising God for this great grace.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
السمنية
البراهمة
تفضل
رحمة
فاعل مختار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because reason can know good and evil, prophets are unnecessary.
Correction: The passage explains that reason often neglects even worldly matters and cannot grasp the subtleties of divine law, which require revelation from a truthful source.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say sending messengers is not obligatory but a favor?
A) Because God is a free agent who is not compelled.
B) Because the intellect is sufficient.
C) Because humans don't need prophets.
D) Because the Mu'tazila were mistaken.

Key Takeaway
Sending messengers is a manifestation of Allah's grace and mercy, not a requirement upon Him, as He is the free agent and reason cannot grasp all truths.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If sending messengers is a favor from Allah, not something He owes you, how does that change your gratitude for having received the message of Islam? What are you doing today to show thanks for that favor?
?
The author says reason alone often fails even in worldly matters. In what area of your life have you relied on your own reasoning and ignored divine guidance? What will you do about it?
?
Do you treat Allah's guidance as a debt He owes you, or as a free gift? How would your daily practice differ if you truly saw every prophetic teaching as a mercy?

Belief in the Prophets Mentioned in the Quran
Dardeer states the obligation to believe in prophets and lists those named in the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to believe in prophets, distinguishing between detailed belief in those named in the Quran and general belief in others.

Core Idea
We must believe in each named prophet individually and in all prophets collectively.

Having established the foundational principles of theology, Dardeer now turns to the Samiyyat—matters known from revelation. He begins with prophethood, affirming the obligation to believe in all prophets. However, he distinguishes between those whose names have been revealed and those who remain unnamed. This passage clarifies how our faith in the prophets is structured: detailed for the known ones, and general for the rest.

Guided Path
1

It balances specific knowledge with general affirmation.

The phrase 'in detail regarding those known by detailed belief' means that for the prophets explicitly named in revelation, a Muslim must believe in each individually. For other prophets whose existence is known in general but whose names are not mentioned, belief in the general category of prophethood suffices. The footnote reference (4) indicates additional commentary not included here.

Faith in the Prophets: Detailed and General Belief
Dardeer explains the obligation to believe in prophets in detail for known ones and in general for others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic obligation to believe in prophets, distinguishing between detailed belief for those named in the Quran and general belief for the rest.

Core Idea
Believe in each named prophet in detail, and in all others in general.

Dardeer explains that while we must believe in all prophets sent by Allah, the level of detail in our belief varies. For the prophets explicitly mentioned in the Quran, we must know and believe in them individually. For all other prophets, a general belief that Allah sent them suffices. This passage clarifies that distinction.

There are 124,000 prophets total.
