The Quranic Principle: Not All Prophets Are Mentioned
Dardeer cites Quran 40:78 to argue against fixing the number of prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran does not specify the exact number of prophets and the rational risk in attempting to do so.

Core Idea
The Quran itself leaves the count open, so we must follow suit.

The author begins by establishing a principle: it is better not to fix the number of prophets. He grounds this directly in the Quran, showing that Allah Himself chose not to enumerate all prophets. Then he highlights a logical risk: any fixed number could wrongly include or exclude a true prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how the author uses the Quran as his primary authority.
2
Identify the Quranic evidence
Find the verse cited (Ghafir 40:78) and understand its implication: not all prophets are mentioned.
The verse is from Surah Ghafir, verse 78.
3
Analyze the rational risk
The author presents two possibilities: saying too many (including false) or too few (missing true prophets). Understand why these risks make specification problematic.
4
Reflect on the principle
Think about why the Quranic openness and the rational risk together make it prudent to avoid fixing a number.
This lesson sets the foundation for the next on hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأولى ترْكُ حضرهم في عددٍ مُعيَّن؛ لقوله تعالى: مِنْهُم مَّن قَصَصْنَا عَلَيْكَ وَمِنْهُمْ مَّن لم نَقْصُص، ولا يؤمَنُ فِي ذِكْرِ العَدَدِ أنْ يُدْخَلَ فيهم مَنْ لَيسَ لَجَوازِ أَنْ يُذْكَرَ أكثَرُ مِنَ الواقع، أو يُخْرَجَ منهم مَن هو منهم إنْ كانَ العدَدُ أَقَلَّ . وما رُوِيَ أنَّ النبيَّ الله سُئِلَ عنْ عددهم فقال: (مائة ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفًا)، وفي رواية (مائتا ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفًا) فخبَرُ أَحادِ لا يفيدُ القطع، ولا عبرة بالظَّنِّ في باب الاعتقاداتِ.
The preferable is to leave off specifying them in a fixed number because of His statement—may He be exalted: 'Of them are some We have told you of and of them are some We have not told you of' [Ghafir 78]. And one cannot be safe in mentioning the number from including among them one who is not of them due to the possibility that one may mention more than the actual, or excluding from them one who is of them if the number is less. And what is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ was asked about their number and he said: 'One hundred and twenty-four thousand' and in another narration 'Two hundred and twenty-four thousand', so it is a hadith of ahad that does not yield certainty, and there is no regard for conjecture in the chapter of beliefs.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage shifts to the question of the exact number of prophets. The author (Dardeer) advises that it is best not to specify a particular number. He supports this with the Quranic verse from Surah Ghafir (40:78) which says some prophets are mentioned and some are not. Specifying a number risks either including someone who is not a prophet or excluding a real prophet. As for the hadith reports that give numbers like 124,000 or 224,000, these are ahad (single-chain) narrations, which only yield probable knowledge (ظن), not certainty (قطع). In matters of belief (اعتقادات), probable knowledge is not sufficient; certainty is required. Therefore one should refrain from committing to a specific number.

Key Terms
عدد الأنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Quran lists all prophets or that we must know the exact number.
Correction: The Quran explicitly says some prophets are not mentioned, so we cannot know the exact number.

Checkpoint
What is the primary Quranic evidence used to argue against specifying the number of prophets?
A) Surah Al-Anbiya 21:101
B) Surah Ghafir 40:78
C) Surah Al-Imran 3:84
D) Surah An-Nisa 4:150

Key Takeaway
The Quran itself does not enumerate all prophets, and any attempt to fix a number risks error, so it is best to avoid specifying.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you been tempted to claim certainty about a religious matter where Allah has remained silent? How does this verse call you to humble your knowledge?
?
Are there beliefs you hold about the unseen that rest on human speculation rather than clear revelation? Will you examine them today and let go of what is not from Allah?
?
If you were to apply the principle of leaving matters open where Allah has left them open, what might change in how you practice or teach your faith? What is one step you can take to align with that this week?

Ahad Hadith Do Not Yield Certainty in Belief
Dardeer explains that prophetic numbers from ahad hadith are not certain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why ahad hadith about the number of prophets are not sufficient for establishing a belief.

Core Idea
Ahad hadith only give probability, and belief requires certainty.

Having established the rational and Quranic basis to avoid fixing a number, the author now addresses the hadith that do mention a number. He explains that these narrations are ahad, meaning they have limited chains of transmission, and thus do not produce certainty (qat'). In matters of belief, probability (zann) is not acceptable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the two reported numbers: 124,000 and 224,000.
2
Understand 'khabar ahad'
The author classifies the hadith as ahad. Learn what this means: a narration that does not reach the level of tawatur.
Ahad hadith are not definitively proven.
3
Grasp the epistemological principle
The author states that such narrations do not yield certainty (qat') and that conjecture (zann) is not considered in matters of belief.
This is a key principle in Islamic theology: belief must be based on certainty.
4
Apply to the issue
Since the hadith only gives probability, we cannot base a firm belief about the number of prophets on it. Therefore, the earlier recommendation to avoid specifying stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

This passage shifts to the question of the exact number of prophets. The author (Dardeer) advises that it is best not to specify a particular number. He supports this with the Quranic verse from Surah Ghafir (40:78) which says some prophets are mentioned and some are not. Specifying a number risks either including someone who is not a prophet or excluding a real prophet. In matters of belief (اعتقادات), probable knowledge is not sufficient; certainty is required. Therefore one should refrain from committing to a specific number.

The Obligation to Believe in Muhammad's Superiority and the Hierarchy of Prophets and Angels
Dardeer states the obligation to believe in Muhammad's superiority and finality, and outlines the prophetic and angelic hierarchy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic obligation to believe in the superiority and finality of Prophet Muhammad and the ranked hierarchy of prophets and angels after him, as taught by Imam Dardeer.

Core Idea
Muhammad is the best and last; then follows a divinely ordered hierarchy.

This passage from Imam Dardeer's commentary establishes a core belief: that Muhammad is the most excellent of all prophets and the final prophet. It then lays out a clear ranking of the other prophets and angels, from the messengers of firm resolve down to the rest of the angels. This hierarchy is not arbitrary but is a matter of obligatory belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic text carefully, then the literal translation. Notice the key terms like 'أفضلهم' (most excellent) and 'آخِرهم' (last).
The passage begins with 'ويجب اعتقاد' – it is obligatory to believe.
2
Identify the hierarchical order
Find the sequence: Muhammad, then ulul 'azm, then rest of messengers, then prophets, then chiefs of angels, then rest of angels. Note that the text says 'without specification' because the true reality is unknown.
3
Understand the obligation
Reflect on why this belief is obligatory (واجب). It is a matter of faith to accept this ranking, even if we don't know the exact details of excellence.
This is part of the 'samiyyat' – matters heard from revelation.
4
Ask: Why this hierarchy?
Consider the theological significance: prophets are superior to angels, and among prophets, Muhammad is best. This ranking affirms his unique status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب اعتقاد أَنَّ مُحمّدًا - صلى الله عليه وسلم وعليهم أجمعين - أفضلُهم) وأنه آخِرُهم)، ويليه في الفضل أولو العزم () مِنَ الرُّسُلِ، فبقيَّةُ الرُّسُلِ، فالأنبياء، فرؤساء الملائكة، فبقيةُ الملائكة مِنْ غَيْرِ تعيين إذ لا تُعلَمُ الحقيقةُ
And it is obligatory to believe that Muhammad—peace be upon him and upon them all—is the most excellent of them and that he is the last of them. And after him in excellence are the messengers of firm resolve (ulul 'azm) from among the messengers, then the rest of the messengers, then the prophets, then the chiefs of the angels, then the rest of the angels, without specification since the reality is not known.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage lays down a hierarchy in the believing community. First, it is obligatory (واجب) to believe that Muhammad is the best (أفضلهم) and the last (آخره). Then the next in rank are the 'ulu al-'azm (messengers of firm resolve) among the messengers. Then the rest of the messengers, then the prophets (who are not messengers), then the chiefs of the angels (like Jibril etc.), then the rest of the angels. However, the exact ranking within each category is not specified (من غير تعيين) because the true reality (الحقيقة) is not known to us. This hierarchy reflects the Ash'ari position that prophets are superior to angels, but among prophets, Muhammad is best, then ulul 'azm, etc. Note: the text does not mention the superiority of prophets over angels explicitly but the order implies it.

Key Terms
أفضلهم
آخِرهم
أولو العزم
الرسل
الأنبياء
الملائكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that all prophets and angels are equal in rank, or that angels are superior to prophets.
Correction: This passage establishes a clear hierarchy: Muhammad is best, then ulul 'azm messengers, then other messengers, then prophets (non-messengers), then angels (chiefs then rest). Prophets as a whole are ranked above angels.

Checkpoint
Who are considered the most excellent after Prophet Muhammad according to this passage?
A) The rest of the messengers.
B) The prophets who are not messengers.
C) The chiefs of the angels.
D) The messengers of firm resolve (ulu al-'azm).

Key Takeaway
It is obligatory to believe that Muhammad is the most excellent and final prophet, and after him comes a defined ranking of prophets and angels, though the exact specifics are not fully known.

?

?

The Hierarchy of the Best of Creation
Dardir enumerates the obligatory belief in the hierarchy of the best creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the divinely established hierarchy of merit among prophets and angels, and why belief in this order is obligatory.

Core Idea
Muhammad is the best of creation, followed by a specific rank order of prophets and angels.

Imam Dardir presents a clear doctrinal statement on the ranking of the best of creation. This hierarchy is not arbitrary but based on divine wisdom. Understanding this order helps avoid common misconceptions about the status of angels versus prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the structure: obligation stated first, then the ordered list.
The passage is a single sentence with several parts.
2
Identify Each Rank
List the categories in the hierarchy from highest to lowest: 1) Muhammad, 2) Ulu al-Azm messengers, 3) Rest of messengers, 4) Prophets, 5) Chiefs of angels, 6) Rest of angels.
Note that 'messengers' are a subset of prophets with a higher rank.
3
Reflect on the Order's Significance
Ask yourself: Why is it important to believe in this order? How does it correct the misconception that angels are superior to prophets?
This hierarchy affirms the superiority of the best humans over angels.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب اعتقادُ أَنَّ مُحمّدًا - صلى الله عليه وسلم وعليهم أجمعين - أفضلُهم) وأنه آخِرُهم)، ويليه في الفضل أولو العزم () مِنَ الرُّسُلِ، فبقيَّةُ الرُّسُلِ، فالأنبياء، فرؤساء الملائكة، فبقيةُ الملائكة مِنْ غَيْرِ تعيين إذ لا تُعلَمُ الحقيقةُ
And it is obligatory to believe that Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace and all of them, is the best of them and that he is the last of them, and next in merit are the ulu al-azm (those of firm resolve) from among the messengers, then the rest of the messengers, then the prophets, then the chiefs of the angels, then the rest of the angels, without specification since the reality is not known.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement on the hierarchy of beings. Dardir asserts that belief is obligatory in the following: first, Muhammad (peace be upon him) is the best of all prophets and is the final prophet. Then, in order of merit come: 1) the ulu al-azm (messengers of firm resolve), 2) the remaining messengers, 3) the prophets (who are not messengers?), 4) the chiefs of angels, and 5) the rest of angels. This order is without a detailed specification of degrees because the exact reality of merit is known only to God.

Correction: This passage clarifies that prophets (and especially Muhammad) rank above angels, so the best humans are superior to the best angels.

C) All prophets

Key Takeaway
Muhammad (peace be upon him) is the best of all creation, and the order of merit among prophets and angels is fixed by divine decree, with prophets ranking above angels.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The hierarchy places prophets above angels. If your heart is drawn more to the angels (e.g., their worship) than to following the prophetic path, what does that reveal about your spiritual orientation? How can you realign yourself with the order that Allah has established?
?
The passage says we affirm the hierarchy without knowing the exact details. Are you comfortable with this divinely placed mystery, or do you find yourself seeking unnecessary distinctions? How can you increase your trust in Allah's wisdom and your humility before His decree?

The Physical Ascension of the Prophet (Mi'raj)
Dardeer describes the physical ascension of the Prophet as a specific example of widely known transmitted matters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specifics of the Prophet's physical ascension (Mi'raj) and its distinction from the Isra journey.

Core Idea
The Mi'raj was a physical, bodily ascension while awake.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer describes the Mi'raj as a specific example of widely known transmitted matters. He clarifies that the ascension was with the Prophet's body while awake, accompanied by Jibreel, and that it occurred after the Isra journey. Understanding these details helps affirm the reality of this miraculous event.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the author's words set the foundation before analysis.
Pay attention to key terms like المعراج and الإسراء.
2
Identify key details of the Mi'raj
Notice that the Mi'raj is described as being with the noble body while awake, with Jibreel, and without the Buraq. This distinguishes it from a spiritual vision.
3
Distinguish between Isra and Mi'raj
Understand that the Isra was a night journey on the Buraq from Mecca to Jerusalem, while the Mi'raj was the ascent to heaven after that, without the Buraq.
Dardeer says the Mi'raj encompasses the Isra (والمراد بالمعراج ما يعم الإسراء).
4
Reflect on the significance
The story is well-known and transmitted widely, making belief in it obligatory. Consider why the physical nature is important for theology.
This guards against interpretations that the Mi'raj was only spiritual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكالمعراج بجَسَدِه الشريف صلى الله عليه وسلم يقظة، وهو العُروجُ إلى السماء معَ جبريل عليه السلام بلا بُراق، بعد الإسراء ليلا مِنَ المسجد الحرام إلى المسجد الأقصى راكبًا للبراق، وهو دابّة أبيضُ طويلٌ، فَوقَ الحِمارِ، ودونَ البَغَلِ، يَضَعُ حافِرَه عِندَ مُنتهى طرفه . والمراد بالمعراج ما يعم الإسراء، وقصته مشهورة.
And also the Mi'raj (ascension) with his noble body, peace be upon him, while awake—it is the ascent to heaven with Jibreel, peace be upon him, without a Buraq, after the Isra (night journey) by night from the Sacred Mosque to the Farthest Mosque, riding the Buraq—and it (the Buraq) is a white, elongated beast, above a donkey and below a mule, placing its hoof at the furthest limit of its sight. And what is meant by al-Mi'raj is that which encompasses al-Isra, and its story is well-known.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the specific example of the Isra and Mi'raj, which is one of the widely known matters that came from the Prophet. The author describes the Mi'raj as the ascension of the Prophet's physical body while awake, with Jibreel, without the Buraq. He notes that this ascension occurred after the Isra, which was a night journey from the Sacred Mosque in Mecca to the Farthest Mosque in Jerusalem, riding the Buraq. The author describes the Buraq as a white, elongated animal, larger than a donkey and smaller than a mule, whose hoof reaches the furthest point of its sight. He then states that the term Mi'raj encompasses both the Isra and the ascension, and that the story is well-known, implying that belief in it is obligatory as part of the widely transmitted matters.

Key Terms

الإسراء
البراق
يقظة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Mi'raj was only spiritual or a dream.
Correction: The author explicitly states it was with the physical body (بجَسَدِه الشريف) and while awake (يقظة), affirming its physical reality.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, was the Mi'raj accompanied by the Buraq?
A) Yes, the Buraq was used for both the Isra and the Mi'raj
B) No, the Mi'raj was without the Buraq
C) The Buraq was used only for the Mi'raj
D) The passage does not mention the Buraq

Key Takeaway
The Mi'raj was a bodily ascension while awake, without a Buraq, after the Isra journey, and belief in it is obligatory as a widely transmitted matter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Prophet traveled from Mecca to Jerusalem on a creature that placed its hoof at the limit of its sight. Have you ever felt that your faith journey is limited by what you can imagine, or do you trust Allah's ability to take you beyond your vision?
?
If the Mi'raj was a widely known transmitted matter, do you treat it as a factual event in your daily life, or do you relegate it to a story you learned as a child? How does your belief in the Mi'raj affect your hope for the afterlife?

Prophethood

Entailments of Prophethood: The Prophet's Attributes
Dardeer enumerates the necessary attributes of the Prophet entailed by his prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the testimony 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' necessitates specific attributes of the Prophet: truthfulness, trustworthiness, conveyance, intelligence, and infallibility, while allowing human accidents that do not diminish his rank.

Core Idea
The second Shahada implies a set of necessary attributes for the Prophet.

The second part of the shahada is not just a declaration; it carries profound implications about the Prophet's character and role. Imam Dardeer explains that from the establishment of Muhammad's prophethood, several attributes necessarily follow. These attributes are not optional but are logically entailed by the very concept of being a messenger. Let's explore what these entailments are.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the word 'يستلزم' as a connector.
2
Identify the six entailments
The passage presents six attributes that are necessitated by prophethood. Find each one: truthfulness, trustworthiness, conveyance, intelligence, infallibility, and the permissibility of human accidents.
3
Understand why each attribute is necessary
For each attribute, think about what would be missing if the Prophet lacked it. For example, if he were not truthful, his message would be unreliable.
Infallibility ensures he does not err in conveying the message.
4
Note the distinction between necessary and permissible
Observe that while certain attributes are necessary, other human characteristics are only permissible as long as they do not lower his rank. This balances his humanity and prophethood.
This prevents extremes of divinizing prophets or reducing them to ordinary men.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الجملة الثانية: وهي قولنا «مُحمّدٌ رسولُ اللهِ» فقد دلّتْ على ثبوتِ الرسالة له ، وذلك يستلزمُ صِدْقَه في كُلِّ ما أخبَرَ به، وأمانته، وتبليغه للعِبادِ كُلَّ ما أمرَ بتبليغه مِنَ الأحكام، وفطانته، إذ الرسولُ لا يكون إلا معصوما، واستحالة أضدادها عليه ، وجَوازَ كُلَّ ما لا يؤدّي إلى نقص في عُلُوّ مُرْتَبتِه مِنَ الأعراض البشريّةِ. ووجوبُ صِدقِه يستلْزِمُ الإيمان بكُلِّ ما جاء به، ومِنْ ذلكَ إرسالُ الرُّسُل (۱)، وهو يستلْزِمُ ما يجبُ في حقهم، وما يستحيل وما يجوز، والإيمان بسائرِ الكُتُبِ السماوية، واليَومِ الآخِرِ ، والحِسابِ، وما عليه ما مرَّ مِنْ جميع السمعيّاتِ.
ولِتَضَمُّنِها جميعَ عقائدِ الإيمانِ جعَلَها الشارع ترجمةً على ما في القلب، ولم يقبل مِنْ أَحَدٍ الإسلام إلا بها، ومِنْ ثَمَّ كانتْ أفضل الأذكار ، قال : (أفضلُ ما قُلتُه أنا والنبيُّونَ مِنْ قبلي لا إلهَ إلا الله) (۲)، وقد ورد في فضلها أحاديثُ كثيرة، ولذلك اختارها السادة الصوفية في السلوكِ إلى الله تعالى على غَيرها مِنَ الأذكار.
And as for the second sentence, which is our saying 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah,' it indicates the establishment of messengership for him, and that necessitates his truthfulness in everything he informed of, his trustworthiness, his conveying to the servants all that he was commanded to convey of rulings, and his intelligence, for the messenger is only infallible, and the impossibility of their opposites for him, and the permissibility of everything that does not lead to a deficiency in the loftiness of his rank from human accidents. And the necessity of his truthfulness necessitates faith in everything he brought, and from that is the sending of messengers, and that necessitates what is necessary regarding them, what is impossible, and what is permissible, and faith in all the heavenly books, the Last Day, the Reckoning, and what has passed of all the sam'iyyat (audible matters). And because it encompasses all the beliefs of faith, the Lawgiver made it the expression of what is in the heart, and He does not accept Islam from anyone except with it; hence it is the best of remembrances. He said: 'The best of what I and the prophets before me have said is: la ilaha illa Allah (there is no god but Allah).' And many hadiths have been narrated regarding its virtue, and therefore the Sufi masters chose it in the journey to Allah, may He be exalted, over other remembrances.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the second part of the shahada, 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah.' The author explains that this statement establishes prophethood for Muhammad, and from that follows his truthfulness, trustworthiness, conveyance of rulings, intelligence, and infallibility. It also necessitates denying opposites of these attributes and allowing human characteristics that do not diminish his status. The necessity of his truthfulness then requires belief in everything he brought, including the sending of prophets, the necessary, impossible, and permissible matters regarding them, faith in all scriptures, the Last Day, the Reckoning, and all the sam'iyyat. The passage then notes that because the shahada encompasses all beliefs, it is the expression of inner faith and the condition for acceptance of Islam. It is the best dhikr, as indicated by a hadith, and for this reason the Sufi masters prefer it over other forms of remembrance.

Key Terms
الرسالة
الصدق
الأمانة
التبليغ
الفطانة
العصمة
الأعراض البشرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the second shahada only affirms prophethood without any further implications.
Correction: In fact, it entails a range of necessary attributes that define the Prophet's role and character.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT entailed by the second shahada?
A) Truthfulness
B) Infallibility
C) Wealth
D) Conveyance

Key Takeaway
The second shahada logically requires that the Prophet possesses truthfulness, trustworthiness, conveyance, intelligence, and infallibility, while only human accidents that don't harm his status are permissible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pronounce the second shahada, do you live as if the Prophet's truthfulness covers every single report he brought, including those about the unseen that you cannot verify? Or do you secretly doubt some of his teachings because they are inconvenient? What would it mean for your faith if you rejected even one of his authentic instructions?
?
The Prophet was commanded to convey all rulings without exception. Are you selective in following Islam, taking the parts that suit you and leaving the rest? If the Prophet trusted Allah enough to deliver the complete message, where is your trust in that message being complete and binding?
?
If you truly believe the Prophet was infallible in what he taught, then every command and prohibition he brought is from Allah. Which command are you currently disobeying or making excuses for? How does that disobedience align with your declaration that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah?

Comprehensive Faith and the Virtue of the Shahada
Dardeer shows that belief in the Prophet implies belief in all his teachings, and praises the shahada as the best dhikr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the requirement to believe the Prophet necessitates faith in everything he brought, including the messengers, scriptures, afterlife, and all sam'iyyat, and why the shahada is considered the best form of remembrance.

Core Idea
Accepting Muhammad as messenger requires believing his entire message, making the shahada the foundation of faith.

Having established the attributes of the Prophet, Dardeer now expands the implications of the shahada to the entire content of revelation. If we must believe the Prophet's truthfulness, then we must believe everything he conveyed. This includes not just prophets but scriptures, the Last Day, and all matters reported from the unseen. The passage concludes by explaining why the shahada is the best dhikr and the key to entering Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for this lesson. Notice the logical flow from truthfulness to comprehensive belief.
The word 'يستلزم' appears again, showing the chain of necessity.
2
Trace the logical necessity
Start from 'the necessity of his truthfulness' and see how it leads to faith in everything he brought, then to specific items.
This is a cascading argument.
3
Identify the specific items of faith
List the categories mentioned: sending of messengers (with their attributes), heavenly books, Last Day, Reckoning, and all sam'iyyat.
Sam'iyyat means matters known through revelation.
4
Reflect on why the shahada is the best dhikr
Consider that it encompasses all beliefs, making it the concise expression of faith. The hadith and Sufi practice confirm its superiority.

Implications of the Second Shahada
Dardeer explains the implications of the second shahada for the Prophet's attributes and our beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the full doctrinal implications of testifying that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah.

Core Idea
The second shahada compels belief in the Prophet's attributes and all he conveyed.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer unpacks the second half of the shahada. He shows that this declaration is not a simple statement but carries a chain of necessary consequences about the Prophet's character and the content of his message. This lesson will walk through those implications step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the English translation. Let the flow of Dardeer's argument come through naturally.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the five attributes
Find where Dardeer lists the attributes necessitated by the second shahada: truthfulness, trustworthiness, conveying, intelligence, and infallibility. Notice the logical chain from prophethood to each attribute.
These attributes are all necessary for a messenger.
3
Connect to broader beliefs
See how the obligation of the Prophet's truthfulness leads to faith in all he brought—other messengers, books, the Last Day, and all revealed matters. Understand why the shahada is called comprehensive.
This shows the shahada’s role as the foundation of Islamic creed.

وأمّا الجملةُ الثانيةُ: وهي قولنا «مُحمّدٌ رسولُ اللهِ» فقد دلّتْ على ثبوتِ الرسالة له ، وذلك يستلزمُ صِدْقَه في كُلِّ ما أخبَرَ به، وأمانته، وتبليغه للعِبادِ كُلَّ ما أمرَ بتبليغه مِنَ الأحكام، وفطانته، إذ الرسولُ لا يكون إلا معصوما، واستحالة أضدادها عليه ، وجَوازَ كُلَّ ما لا يؤدّي إلى نقص في عُلُوّ مُرْتَبتِه مِنَ الأعراض البشريّةِ. ووجوبُ صِدقِه يستلْزِمُ الإيمان بكُلِّ ما جاء به، ومِنْ ذلكَ إرسالُ الرُّسُل ()، وهو يستلْزِمُ ما يجبُ في حقهم، وما يستحيل وما يجوز، والإيمان بسائرِ الكُتُبِ السماوية، واليَومِ الآخِرِ ، والحِسابِ، وما عليه ما مرَّ مِنْ جميع السمعيّاتِ. ولِتَضَمُّنِها جميعَ عقائدِ الإيمانِ جعَلَها الشارع ترجمةً على ما في القلب، ولم يقبل مِنْ أَحَدٍ الإسلام إلا بها، ومِنْ ثَمَّ كانتْ أفضل الأذكار ، قال : (أفضلُ ما قُلتُه أنا والنبيُّونَ مِنْ قبلي لا إلهَ إلا الله) (۲)، وقد ورد في فضلها أحاديثُ كثيرة، ولذلك اختارها السادة الصوفية في السلوكِ إلى الله تعالى على غَيرها مِنَ الأذكار.
As for the second sentence, which is our saying 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah,' it indicates the establishment of prophethood (risālah) for him, and that necessitates his truthfulness (ṣidq) in everything he informed about, his trustworthiness (amānah), his conveying to the servants everything he was commanded to convey of the rulings (aḥkām), and his intelligence (faṭānah), because the messenger (rasūl) is only infallible (ma‘ṣūm), and the impossibility of their opposites for him, and the permissibility (jawāz) of everything that does not lead to a deficiency in the loftiness of his rank from human accidents (a‘rāḍ bashariyyah). And the obligation (wujūb) of his truthfulness necessitates faith (īmān) in everything he brought, and from that is the sending of messengers, and it necessitates what is obligatory (wājib) regarding them, what is impossible (mustaḥīl), and what is permissible (jā’iz), and faith in all the heavenly books, the Last Day, the Reckoning, and all the sam‘iyyāt (matters known through revelation) that have passed. And because it comprises all the beliefs (ʿaqā’id) of faith, the Lawgiver made it an expression of what is in the heart, and He does not accept Islam from anyone except with it, and therefore it is the best of remembrances (adhkār). He said (alayhi al-salāh wa al-salām): 'The best of what I and the prophets before me have said is Lā ilāha illā Allāh.' And many hadiths have been reported regarding its virtue, and therefore the masters of Sufism (al-sādah al-ṣūfiyyah) chose it in the path (sulūk) to Allah Most High over other remembrances.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the doctrinal implications of the second part of the shahada, 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah.' Dardeer begins by stating that this declaration indicates the establishment of prophethood for the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). From this established prophethood, several necessary consequences follow: his truthfulness in all that he reported, his trustworthiness, his complete conveying of all the rulings he was commanded to deliver, and his intelligence—because a messenger must be infallible, and all opposites of these attributes are impossible for him. Additionally, it entails the permissibility of anything from human accidents that does not detract from the loftiness of his rank. Dardeer then explains that the obligation of his truthfulness logically requires faith in everything he brought. This includes faith in the sending of other messengers, which in turn requires belief in what is obligatory, impossible, and permissible regarding them, faith in all the heavenly books, the Last Day, the Reckoning, and all the sam‘iyyāt (revealed doctrines) that have been mentioned. The passage then explains why the shahada encompasses all beliefs of faith, making it the best form of remembrance. The Lawgiver (Allah) made it the expression of what is in the heart and accepts Islam only through it. Dardeer cites the hadith: 'The best of what I and the prophets before me have said is Lā ilāha illā Allāh,' and notes that many hadiths attest to its virtue, which is why the Sufi masters chose it as their primary remembrance in the spiritual journey to Allah.

Key Terms
رسالة (risālah)
صِدق (ṣidq)
أمانة (amānah)
فطانة (faṭānah)
عصمة (‘iṣmah)
جواز (jawāz)
سمعيات (sam‘iyyāt)
ذكر (dhikr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The second shahada is merely a verbal statement with no further implications.
Correction: Dardeer shows that it entails a wide range of doctrinal beliefs about the Prophet and his message.

Checkpoint
According to Dardeer, the second shahada necessitates which of the following regarding the Prophet?
A) Only his truthfulness
B) Only his trustworthiness
C) Both his truthfulness and infallibility, among other attributes
D) Only his conveying of rulings

Key Takeaway
The second shahada is the foundation of Islamic belief, necessitating faith in the Prophet's perfect attributes and all that he conveyed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every single thing the Prophet (peace be upon him) conveyed—including matters of the unseen, the afterlife, and the details of past nations—is absolutely true? If there is any doubt in your heart, what does that say about the sincerity of your shahada? Will you seek certainty until it becomes a reality for you?
?
The Prophet said the best remembrance is 'La ilaha illa Allah,' yet the shahada includes his messengerhood. How often do you consciously recite the full shahada with presence of heart, understanding that it obligates you to believe in the Prophet's infallibility and all he brought? Will you make it your daily spiritual practice starting today?
?
This passage teaches that the second shahada requires faith in all the heavenly books and messengers. Is there any prophet or scripture you feel uneasy about or don't fully accept? What step will you take to remove that unease and submit completely to what the Prophet has taught?
